| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-02 | Numeric primitives — number→i32/i64/f64 inference + arithmetic ops | Lower TS `number` to the right WASM numeric type. Inference policy (closed by `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-NUMERIC-001`): use ts-morph's typechecker contextual-type read at each numeric expression; integer-typed numbers (typechecker `getTypeAtLocation` + heuristic — "all uses are `Math.floor`/integer-bitops/array-index" — yields i32 for tight ranges and i64 otherwise) lower to i32/i64; floating-point (any `/` operator on numbers, or `Math.{sqrt,sin,cos,log,...}` use, or explicit `Number.isFinite` paths) lowers to f64. When ambiguous, default to f64 with a documented downgrade warning. Ops covered: `+ - * / %` (numeric), `== != < <= > >=` (returns i32 boolean), `& | ^ << >> >>> ~` (forces i32). **Acceptance:** parity vs ts-backend on 10 property-based numeric substrates spanning the 3 numeric domains (4 i32, 3 i64, 3 f64); each ≥20 fast-check cases byte-equivalent (or value-equality with documented float-tolerance for f64). The wave-2 demo numeric `it()` slot extended with 3 new property-based cases. `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-01 | review | not started — blocked on WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-01 |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-03 | Booleans + comparisons + branches | Lower TS `boolean` to WASM i32 (0/1). Lower `&&` / `\|\|` / `!` with short-circuit semantics (must emit `if`/`else` block opcodes — short-circuit observable when RHS has side effects on local state). Lower comparison ops (`==`, `===`, `!=`, `!==`, `<`, `<=`, `>`, `>=`) returning i32. **`==` vs `===` policy** (closed by implementer @decision `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-EQ-001`): both ops well-typed under strict-subset; lowering can emit identical opcodes for primitives (object-equality out of scope until WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-06). **Acceptance:** parity vs ts-backend on 8 boolean/comparison substrates (boolean ops, short-circuit-with-side-effect, integer comparisons across i32/i64/f64, mixed numeric comparisons), each ≥15 property-based cases. `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-02 | review | not started — blocked on WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-02 |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-04 | bigint → i64 with overflow semantics | Lower TS `bigint` (literals like `123n` and `BigInt(...)` calls) to WASM i64. Lower bigint arithmetic and bitops. **Overflow policy** (closed by implementer @decision `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-BIGINT-001`): JS `bigint` is arbitrary-precision; WASM i64 is 64-bit two's-complement. Recommended (a) emit i64 ops and document overflow truncation as a deliberate v1 simplification — keeps host contract closed at `WASM_HOST_CONTRACT.md`. Alternative (b) host-mediate via `host_bigint_*` imports (defers to v1-wave-4). **Acceptance:** parity vs ts-backend on 5 bigint substrates (basic arithmetic, bitops, mixed-with-number forced to bigint, edge values at i64 min/max). At least 1 substrate exercises the overflow boundary explicitly. `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-02 | review | not started — blocked on WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-02 |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-05 | Strings — UTF-8 linear-memory representation + length, indexOf, slice, concat | Lower TS `string` to a linear-memory layout: `(ptr: i32, len_bytes: i32)` pair on the stack (consistent with WASM-03 host contract — `host_alloc(size)` returns ptr; the wave-2 host's UTF-8 reader is wired). String literals serialize to the data section. Methods: `.length` (char count, NOT byte count — UTF-16 surrogate-aware policy `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-STR-001`: emit host call `host_string_length(ptr, len_bytes) → i32 char_count`), `.indexOf` (host-mediated `host_string_indexof`), `.slice(start, end?)` (linear-memory copy via `host_alloc`), template literals (concat via `host_alloc` + `memory.copy`), `+` operator on strings (delegates to concat), `===`/`!==` (byte-compare two `(ptr, len)` pairs). **Host contract amendment**: new imports `host_string_length`, `host_string_indexof` added to `WASM_HOST_CONTRACT.md` (wave-3 amendment, version-bumped per existing versioning section). **Acceptance:** the wave-2 demo `string` `it.todo()` slot is activated; parity vs ts-backend on 6 string substrates (length, indexOf, slice, concat, template, equality), each ≥15 property-based cases. `WASM_HOST_CONTRACT.md` version bumped (host implementation extended). `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-01, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-03 | approve | not started — gated on host-contract amendment |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-06 | Records — flat-struct linear-memory layout + field access | Lower TS object-literal records (`{ a: number, b: number }` and similar nominally-typed records via `interface`/`type`) to flat-struct in linear memory. **Layout policy** (closed by implementer @decision `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-LAYOUT-001`): 8-byte alignment per field (uniform, makes field offsets trivially `field_index * 8`); little-endian per WASM spec; records-by-value pass `(ptr, _struct_size)` on the stack with `host_alloc` for the struct body. Field access lowers to `i32.load`/`i64.load`/`f64.load` at `(ptr + field_offset)` per the field's lowered numeric type. Nested records lower recursively. **Acceptance:** parity vs ts-backend on 5 record substrates (sum-of-fields-numeric, record-of-strings, nested-record, record-with-mixed-numeric-types, record-equality). The wave-2 demo `mixed` `it.todo()` slot is activated. `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-02, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-05 | review | not started — blocked on numeric + string lowering |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-07 | Arrays — length+ptr+capacity representation + indexing, length, push | Lower TS array `T[]` to `(ptr: i32, length: i32, capacity: i32)` triple in linear memory. **Element stride policy** (closed by implementer @decision `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-ARRAY-001`): stride = the element type's lowered size (i32→4, i64→8, f64→8, string→8 for `(ptr, len)`-pair, record→8 for ptr-to-struct). Operations: `arr[i]` indexing, `.length`, `.push(x)` (grows via `host_alloc` + `memory.copy` when capacity exhausted; doubles capacity each grow). `.map(fn)`/`.filter(fn)` deferred to WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-10 (require closures). `for-of` over arrays desugars to indexed `for` in WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-08. **Acceptance:** parity vs ts-backend on 6 array substrates (sum, indexing, length, push, push-with-grow, mixed-element-type via record-elements). `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-06 | review | not started — blocked on records (record-of-array exercises both) |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-08 | Control flow — if/else, while, for, for-of, switch, return, try/catch | Lower the full strict-subset-accepted control flow surface. `if/else` → `if`/`else`/`end` block opcodes. `while` → `loop` + `br_if`. `for (init; cond; post)` → desugar to `init; while (cond) { body; post }`. `for-of` over arrays → indexed `for` over `.length`. `for-of` over strings → host-mediated char iteration. `switch` with literal cases → `br_table` when integer literals; chained `if/else if` otherwise. `return` → `return` opcode. **try/catch policy** (closed by implementer @decision `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-TRY-001`): recommended (a) emit `try`/`catch_all` opcodes per WASM EH proposal (modern Node/Chrome/Firefox implement); alternative (b) host-mediated `setjmp`-shaped pattern via `host_panic`. Recommended (a). **Acceptance:** parity vs ts-backend on 8 control-flow substrates (if/else, while-loop, for-loop, for-of-array, for-of-string, switch-with-integer-cases, switch-with-string-cases, try-catch-with-throw), each ≥15 property-based cases. `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-03, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-07 | review | not started — blocked on booleans + arrays |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-09 | Function calls — intra-module direct + host-mediated I/O | Intra-module calls lower to WASM `call <funcidx>` — visitor builds a function index table during scaffold and resolves calls at lowering time, two-pass for forward-references. Host-mediated I/O calls (anything matching `host_*` import surface) lower to `call <import_funcidx>`. Recursive calls work by construction. **Calls to functions outside the resolution result MUST fail loudly** per Sacred Practice #5. **Acceptance:** parity vs ts-backend on 5 call substrates (direct call, recursive call — factorial/fib, indirect via record-of-functions [DEFERRED to WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-10 if it requires closures], call with multiple args of mixed types, call returning a record). `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-08 | review | not started — blocked on control flow (recursion exercises both) |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-10 | Closures + higher-order functions — lambda-lifting | Strict-subset accepts closures (well-typed and pure if captured state is). **Strategy decision** (closed by implementer @decision `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-CLOSURE-001`): three options — (a) support directly via `(funcref, env_ptr)` representation in linear memory + `call_indirect`; (b) **lambda-lift** at lowering time — analyze captured-variable set, hoist closure to a top-level function with captures threaded as explicit additional parameters; (c) reject closures (violates "anything strict-subset accepts is in scope"). Recommended **(b)**: works because under the strict-subset all bindings are lexical and `let`/`const` are statically resolvable; produces standard top-level WASM functions (no `call_indirect` complexity). After this WI: WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-07 `.map`/`.filter` slots activated; WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-09 indirect-via-record-of-functions substrate activated. **Acceptance:** parity vs ts-backend on 6 closure substrates (basic closure, multi-local capture across nested scopes, higher-order with `.map`, higher-order with `.filter`, returns-a-closure, mutual recursion via closures). `pnpm --filter @yakcc/compile test` passes; `pnpm -r build` clean. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-09 | approve | not started — gated on call surface |
| WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-11 | Property-based parity harness over yakcc-self-shave corpus + wave-3 closer | Wave-3 closer demo. Extend `examples/v1-wave-2-wasm-demo/` (or create sibling `examples/v1-wave-3-wasm-lower-demo/` per implementer's `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-DEMO-001`) with a property-based harness driving the WASM backend over the **yakcc-self-shave corpus** — the 118-atom corpus produced by `node packages/cli/dist/bin.js bootstrap` (WI-V2-BOOTSTRAP-02/-03), the largest realistic strict-subset-conformant corpus we have. Harness: (i) reads `bootstrap/expected-roots.json`, (ii) for each atom builds a synthetic `ResolutionResult` (atom + sub-block deps if glue), (iii) compiles via both backends, (iv) executes both compiled artifacts against the same property-based input set (≥20 fast-check cases per atom), (v) asserts byte-equivalent output (or value-equality with documented float-tolerance for f64-output atoms). Atoms requiring host capabilities the wave-3 lowering does not yet implement marked `pending` (NOT silent-skip, Sacred Practice #5 / WI-V1W2-WASM-04 precedent). **Acceptance:** harness runs to completion against ≥80% of corpus (≥94 of 118 atoms), remaining ≤20% explicitly listed `pending` with per-atom reason. ≥20 property-based cases per non-pending atom. Demo invocable via `pnpm --filter v1-wave-3-wasm-lower-demo test` (or wave-2 demo's harness — implementer picks); CI runs every commit. `pnpm -r build` clean. **This is the v1 wave-3 closer**: when this lands, v1 wave-3 closes per `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-LOWER-001` and the WI-V1W2-WASM-02 supersedence is fully realized. **Scope hint:** `examples/v1-wave-3-wasm-lower-demo/` (new, OR extension of `examples/v1-wave-2-wasm-demo/`); no source-code edits to `packages/*/`. Pre-assigned decision: `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-DEMO-001`. | WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-05, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-06, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-07, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-08, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-09, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-10 | approve | not started — wave-3 closer; gated on full lowering surface |

v1 wave-3 dependency map: **W1** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-01}` (scaffold; fully unblocked off main at `38bd542`). **W2** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-02}` after scaffold. **W3** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-03, WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-04}` parallel after numeric (booleans and bigint disjoint). **W4** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-05}` after WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-03 (strings need host-contract amendment). **W5** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-06}` after strings. **W6** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-07}` after records. **W7** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-08}` after arrays. **W8** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-09}` after control flow. **W9** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-10}` after calls. **W10** = `{WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-11}` after full lowering surface lands. Critical path = 10 sequential waves; max width = 2 (W3). When `WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-11` lands, v1 wave-3 closes; v1 wave-4 candidates (Map/Set, async/await, deferred ≤20% of self-shave corpus, F2+ federation publishing) are planned as a fresh initiative at that point.

### Initiative: v2 self-hosting wave-1 (parallel WI-V2-01 + WI-V2-02)

Status: **active 2026-05-01.** The user authorized two parallel high-leverage v2 W1 dispatches off main at `ba9c55a` (post-WI-033 / continue-break slicer fix). WI-V2-01 (whole-project IR validator mode) is the prerequisite for every other v2 phase per the conformance audit; WI-V2-02 (fix the 4 real IR-conformance violations) is structurally independent and runs in a sister session. The two WIs touch disjoint surfaces (WI-V2-01 in `packages/ir`; WI-V2-02 in `packages/contracts/src/embeddings.ts` + `packages/ir/src/strict-subset-cli.ts` + `packages/cli/src/bin.ts`) so they can execute concurrently without merge conflict. WI-V2-01's self-validation evidence is the input that confirms WI-V2-02's choice of fix sites for the singletons and CLI entry-points.

| ID | Title | Description | Deps | Gate | State |
|----|-------|-------------|------|------|-------|
| WI-V2-01 | Whole-project IR validator mode | Add `validateStrictSubsetProject(tsconfigPath): Promise<ProjectValidationResult>` to `@yakcc/ir` (or, alternatively, a `mode: 'project' \| 'isolated'` option on existing `validateStrictSubset`; implementer picks per `DEC-V2-IR-PROJECT-MODE-001`). The new mode loads a real `tsconfig.json` via ts-morph's `tsConfigFilePath` constructor option and resolves cross-file relative imports, workspace `@yakcc/*` cross-package imports, and `node:*` builtin imports through the actual TypeScript resolver — eliminating the ~98% false-positive `no-untyped-imports` rate seen in isolated mode against whole-package source (per `~/.claude/plans/v2-ir-conformance-audit.md` 2026-05-01). Both modes consume the SAME rule registry (Sacred Practice #12); project mode does NOT relax any substantive rule; the only behavioral difference is that no-untyped-imports stops emitting false positives because real resolution succeeds. Acceptance includes a self-validation pass against `packages/ir/tsconfig.json` producing zero or near-zero false-positive no-untyped-imports while still surfacing the 4 real violations that become WI-V2-02's input. Evaluation Contract: `tmp/eval-wi-v2-01-ir-project-mode.json`. Scope Manifest: `tmp/scope-wi-v2-01-ir-project-mode.json`. Pre-assigned decision: `DEC-V2-IR-PROJECT-MODE-001` (closed by implementer's @decision annotation). | (none — pure additive) | review | landed (impl `a968416`, merge `e972b9c`, 2026-05-01 — DEC-V2-IR-PROJECT-MODE-001; 99/99 IR tests green, 11 new project-mode tests, 5 fixtures across 14 files) |
| WI-V2-02 | Fix the 4 real IR-conformance violations | Two singleton mutables in `packages/contracts/src/embeddings.ts:49,113` (refactor `let` to function-scoped closure or Map cache); two CLI entry-point top-level dispatches in `packages/ir/src/strict-subset-cli.ts:111` and `packages/cli/src/bin.ts:7` (either wrap in `if (import.meta.url === ...) main()` pattern, or relax `no-top-level-side-effects` with a documented `// @cli-entry` exemption captured as `DEC-IR-CLI-ENTRY-EXEMPTION-001`). Implementer picks the strategy per call site at dispatch. Acceptance: WI-V2-01's self-validation pass goes from "4 real violations" to "0 violations" against the same fixed source set. | (none — structurally orthogonal to WI-V2-01) | review | in progress (orchestrator-dispatched 2026-05-01, sister session) |

WI-V2-01 + WI-V2-02 together complete the v2 wave W1 (`{WI-V2-01, WI-V2-02}` per the dependency-wave map below). When both land, WI-V2-03 + WI-V2-04 (W2) become unblocked.

### Initiative: v2 self-hosting

Status: **planned.** Gated on v0.7 closure (WI-015 demo, done) and v1 wave-1 closure (WI-021 federation demo). Detailed phase breakdown landed 2026-05-01 informed by the IR conformance audit (`~/.claude/plans/v2-ir-conformance-audit.md`); WIs are marked "deferred" until both gating demos run.

Today the validator runs in isolated-file mode using a fresh in-memory ts-morph Project per call — fine for block-level seed-corpus validation, but yields ~98% false-positive `no-untyped-imports` violations when run against whole-package source (per audit 2026-05-01). Acceptance: `pnpm test` passes against the recomposed yakcc compiled via `yakcc compile`. **Framing-shift note (WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE, #78, 2026-05-04):** Under the glue-aware framing, yakcc constructs that don't currently shave cleanly become `GlueLeafEntry` rather than hard failures; the recomposed yakcc includes glue regions verbatim. Functional equivalence (`pnpm test` passing) remains the acceptance gate unchanged. **Re-routed 2026-05-10 per `DEC-V2-DISPATCH-REROUTE-001`:** decomposed into three slices `WI-V2-08-A` (harness skeleton), `WI-V2-08-B` (compile-then-test), `WI-V2-08-C` (diff harness) under "Initiative: v2 self-hosting closure" — see that initiative's table for the live ledger. | WI-V2-07 | approve | **in progress — W4+W5 bundled into #59** (Serenity); supersedes original three-slice plan; live row in v2-closure initiative |
| WI-V2-09 | Two-pass bootstrap equivalence (Phase H) | The crown jewel. Take the recomposed yakcc from WI-V2-08, use IT to re-shave the original yakcc source. The resulting block tree must be byte-identical at the `BlockMerkleRoot` level to the WI-V2-07 first-pass blocks. Fixed-point self-hosting: yakcc-N produces yakcc-N+1 produces yakcc-N+1 (no further drift). Any divergence is a non-determinism bug somewhere in the canonicalizer or hashing path — the most valuable test the project can have. Pre-assigned decision: `DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-EQUIV-001`. **Framing-shift note (WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE, #78, 2026-05-04):** The byte-identity assertion now applies separately to `local` atoms (content-addressed, must be byte-identical across passes) and `glue` regions (verbatim-preserved by construction, so byte-identical trivially). Fixed-point self-hosting still holds; glue boundaries reduce the scope of non-determinism risk by making the non-shaveable surface's identity trivial. **Live row in "v2 self-hosting closure" initiative.** | WI-V2-08-C | approve | **filed → #286 (W6)**; live row in v2-closure initiative |
| WI-V2-10 | v2 demo + CI (Phase I) | Document the self-hosting flow at `docs/V2_SELF_HOSTING_DEMO.md`: every command an external person runs, expected outputs, what to do when things diverge. Wire CI to run the WI-V2-09 two-pass equivalence check on every commit so a self-hosting regression never lands silently. This becomes the project's strongest external demo: "the compiler shaves itself, recomposes itself, and the result is byte-identical." **Framing-shift note (WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE, #78, 2026-05-04):** The demo claim sharpens to: "yakcc shaves the meaningfully-reusable parts of arbitrary TS source, including itself — glue regions are preserved verbatim and are byte-identical by construction." This is a more honest and more widely applicable claim; the README and demo language MUST update accordingly when this WI lands. **Live row in "v2 self-hosting closure" initiative.** | WI-V2-09 | approve | **filed → #287 (W7)**; live row in v2-closure initiative |

v2 dependency waves: **W1** = `{WI-V2-01, WI-V2-02}` (parallel; whole-project validator + fix the 4 real violations). **W2** = `{WI-V2-03, WI-V2-04}` (IR extensions + foreign-block primitives, both gated on WI-V2-01). **W3** = `{WI-V2-05, WI-V2-06}` (source refactor + property-test coverage). **W4** = `{WI-V2-07}` (first shave). **W5** = `{WI-V2-08}` (compile self-equivalence). **W6** = `{WI-V2-09}` (two-pass bootstrap). **W7** = `{WI-V2-10}` (demo + CI). Critical path: WI-V2-01 → WI-V2-03 → WI-V2-05 → WI-V2-07 → WI-V2-08 → WI-V2-09 → WI-V2-10. W4+W5 are in progress under #59. W6 filed as #286; W7 filed as #287.

### Initiative: WI-CI-OFFLINE-01 — offline-tolerant tests + general test CI

Status: **active 2026-05-03.** Single-WI initiative seeded by issue #37 ("[Wrath] WI-CI-OFFLINE-01: Migrate tests to offline embedding provider + add general test CI workflow"). Branched off `main` at `c214cf1` (post-WI-V1W3-WASM-LOWER-01 land + post-`createOfflineEmbeddingProvider()` ship at `4d29b30`). Orthogonal to the v1-wave-3 lowering chain (Wrath sister track) and to the v2 self-hosting chain — touches CI infra and test files only, with a single bounded production-source extension on `RunFederationOptions` in `packages/cli/src/commands/federation.ts`. Runtime workflow id: `WI-CI-OFFLINE-01`. Runtime goal id: `g-wi-ci-offline-01`. Runtime work-item id: `wi-ci-offline-01`.

**Two real problems on `main` at `c214cf1`, same root cause, fix primitive already shipped:**

1. **`pnpm -r test` is broken in any network-blocked environment.** `packages/contracts/src/embeddings.test.ts` (the `EmbeddingProvider (local)` describe block at lines 157–209, 9 tests) and `packages/cli/src/commands/federation.test.ts` (8 tests calling `runFederation(["pull", ...])` which transitively opens the registry without an explicit provider) hit `Forbidden access to file: "https://huggingface.co/Xenova/all-MiniLM-L6-v2/resolve/main/tokenizer.json"`. The `:memory:` registry call sites in `cli.test.ts:94`, `assemble-candidate.test.ts:90`, `assemble.test.ts:181`, `resolve.test.ts:130`, and `seed.test.ts:{85,97,111,112,126}` likewise rely on the network-bound default provider.
2. **There is no general test CI workflow.** `.github/workflows/bootstrap.yml` only runs `yakcc bootstrap --verify` (already offline-tolerant via `BOOTSTRAP_EMBEDDING_OPTS`). `pnpm -r test` and `pnpm -r build` are never gated on PRs, so the silent failures in (1) cannot be caught.

**Fix primitive already shipped.** `createOfflineEmbeddingProvider()` lives in `packages/contracts/src/embeddings.ts:118-185` (commit `4d29b30`): no-arg, returns `EmbeddingProvider` with `dimension: 384` and `modelId: "yakcc/offline-blake3-stub"`, deterministic by BLAKE3 + L2-normalized. Re-exported from `@yakcc/contracts/src/index.ts`. The migration is purely call-site: every `openRegistry(...)` / `seedRegistry(...)` site in the failing test files passes `{ embeddings: createOfflineEmbeddingProvider() }`.

**Audit summary on `c214cf1` (test files needing migration, by type of call site):**

- `packages/cli/src/cli.test.ts:94` — `openRegistry(":memory:")` then `seedRegistry(reg)` (1 site).
- `packages/compile/src/assemble-candidate.test.ts:90` — `:memory:` then `storeBlock` (1 site).
- `packages/compile/src/assemble.test.ts:181` — `:memory:` then `storeBlock` (1 site).
- `packages/compile/src/resolve.test.ts:130` — `:memory:` then `storeBlock` (1 site).
- `packages/seeds/src/seed.test.ts:85,97,111,112,126` — `:memory:` then `seedRegistry()` (5 sites).
- `packages/contracts/src/embeddings.test.ts` — gate the `EmbeddingProvider (local)` describe block (lines 157–209, 9 tests) via `describe.skipIf(process.env.YAKCC_NETWORK_TESTS !== "1")`. The 6 `EmbeddingProvider (offline / BLAKE3 stub)` tests in the same file already use the offline factory and run unchanged. **Do NOT delete the local-provider tests** — gating preserves the local-path coverage for opt-in operator runs.
- `packages/cli/src/commands/federation.test.ts` — needs the production-side `RunFederationOptions.embeddings?: EmbeddingProvider` extension in `federation.ts` to land first. The 8 failing tests run `runFederation(["pull", ...])`, which calls bare `openRegistry(dbPath)` inside `federation.ts:145, 237, 346`. The test files alone cannot fix this; the bounded production-side extension threads the optional provider through to those three call sites and the tests pass `embeddings: createOfflineEmbeddingProvider()` as a `runFederation` option.

**The new CI workflow (Part B) — `.github/workflows/test.yml`:**

```yaml
name: test
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
  pull_request:
    branches: [main]
concurrency:
  group: test-${{ github.ref }}
  cancel-in-progress: true
jobs:
  test:
    name: pnpm -r build + test
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    timeout-minutes: 30
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: pnpm/action-setup@v4
      - uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: 22
          cache: pnpm
      - run: pnpm install --frozen-lockfile
      - run: pnpm -r build
      - run: pnpm -r test
```

The `pnpm/action-setup@v4` step carries **no `with: version:` field** — `package.json#packageManager: pnpm@9.15.0` is the single canonical authority for the pnpm version (DEC-CI-OFFLINE-004), mirroring the post-`a9300b2` shape of `bootstrap.yml`.

### Initiative: WI-CI-OFFLINE-03 — lift embeddings injection to runCli top-level (CliOptions)

Status: **active 2026-05-03.** Single-WI architectural-cleanup follow-up to WI-CI-OFFLINE-01. Seeded by issue #43 ("[Wrath] WI-CI-OFFLINE-03: Lift embeddings injection to runCli top-level (CliOptions)"). Branched off `main` at `221a957` (post-WI-CI-OFFLINE-01 land at `1513282` plus WI-CI-OFFLINE-02 land at `221a957`). Sister-persona convention: owned by Wrath (hourly `wrath-poll` cron is currently disabled — no race expected). Runtime workflow id: `WI-CI-OFFLINE-03`. Runtime goal id: `g-wi-ci-offline-03`. Runtime work-item id: `wi-ci-offline-03`.

**Why this WI exists.** WI-CI-OFFLINE-01 made the offline-embedding path work by extending each affected per-command file with an `*Options { embeddings?: RegistryOptions["embeddings"] }` interface (`CompileOptions`, `SearchOptions`, `SeedOptions`, `FederationOptions`) and migrating tests to call those command functions directly via per-command imports (`await seed([...], logger, { embeddings: offlineEmbeddings })`). It works, but it bypasses `runCli` — the canonical CLI entry — for any test that needs to inject embeddings. Every test caller that wants the offline provider has to know which inner command function to import and invoke directly; the central `runCli(...)` dispatch is a dead end for embedding injection. The closed-as-duplicate PR #40 included the small architectural improvement that didn't make it into main: a top-level `CliOptions` interface on `runCli()` itself, so the embedding seam exists once at the entry point and `runCli` forwards it to each command handler that already accepts `{ embeddings }`. This is a clean ~12-LOC lift from PR #40's `index.ts` portion plus at least one converted test in `cli.test.ts`. Salvage worth doing because it restores `runCli` as the canonical test entry.

**Audit on `221a957`.** Per-command options are already wired:
- `packages/cli/src/commands/compile.ts:28` exports `CompileOptions { embeddings?: RegistryOptions["embeddings"] }`; `compile()` accepts `opts?: CompileOptions` and forwards `opts?.embeddings` to `openRegistry`.
- `packages/cli/src/commands/search.ts:22` exports `SearchOptions` with the same shape; `search()` forwards.
- `packages/cli/src/commands/seed.ts:21` exports `SeedOptions` with the same shape; `seed()` forwards.
- `packages/cli/src/commands/federation.ts:66` exports `FederationOptions` with the same shape (plus `transport?` for stub injection); `runFederation()`, `runFederationServe()`, `runFederationMirror()`, `runFederationPull()` all forward.

All four `runCli` switch arms (`compile`, `search`, `seed`, `federation` at `index.ts:155-197`) currently call their inner functions with TWO args (no `opts`). The lift threads `opts?.embeddings` through exactly those four arms. Other arms (`registry init`, `propose`, `query`, `bootstrap`, `shave`, `hooks`, `--help`, default error) are NOT threaded — see Non-Goals below.

**Non-goals (explicit, with rationale).**
1. **NOT threading `embeddings` into `propose`, `query`, `shave`.** These commands DO call `openRegistry(registryPath)` (no embedding option), so they technically remain network-bound if invoked offline. Threading would require adding new `*Options` interfaces inside their command files, which are in `forbidden_paths` for this WI. If a future operator hits offline-broken `propose`/`query`/`shave` tests, file WI-CI-OFFLINE-04 to extend those three commands with the same per-command `*Options { embeddings? }` shape.
2. **NOT threading into `bootstrap`.** `packages/cli/src/commands/bootstrap.ts` is intentionally pinned to `BOOTSTRAP_EMBEDDING_OPTS` (the inline zero-vector pattern) per DEC-CI-OFFLINE-001 and DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-EMBEDDING-001 — it is the canonical authority for the bootstrap-verify path and changing it would re-derive `bootstrap/expected-roots.json` and break the v2 bootstrap demo invariant established by WI-V2-BOOTSTRAP-03.
3. **NOT mass-converting every test.** The acceptance criterion is at-least-one converted test exercising one of the four threaded arms (compile|search|seed|federation) under offline mode. Converting more is permitted for symmetry but not required; rewriting tests that already use the per-command form for unrelated reasons is forbidden.
4. **NOT changing `packages/cli/src/bin.ts`.** The production CLI shim calls `runCli(process.argv.slice(2))` with two args. The new third arg is optional and that path stays unchanged.

| ID | Title | Description | Deps | Gate | State |
|----|-------|-------------|------|------|-------|
| WI-CI-OFFLINE-03 | Lift embeddings injection to runCli top-level (CliOptions) | Add `export interface CliOptions { embeddings?: RegistryOptions["embeddings"]; }` to `packages/cli/src/index.ts` (alongside the existing `Logger` / `CONSOLE_LOGGER` / `CollectingLogger` exports), add `opts?: CliOptions` as the third optional parameter to `runCli`, and thread `{ embeddings: opts?.embeddings }` into exactly the four switch arms whose handlers already accept embeddings: `compile` (line 158), `search` (line 173), `seed` (line 179), `federation` (line 196). The `RegistryOptions` type is imported via `import type { RegistryOptions } from "@yakcc/registry"` so `CliOptions.embeddings` is a strict type-alias of the canonical authority — Sacred Practice #12, single source of truth (DEC-CI-OFFLINE-006). Convert at least one existing `cli.test.ts` test that currently calls a per-command function directly (e.g. `await seed([...], logger, { embeddings: offlineEmbeddings })` at line 198 / 205, or one of the `compile([...], logger, { embeddings })` sites) to call `await runCli([...], logger, { embeddings: offlineEmbeddings })` instead, proving the seam end-to-end under offline mode. **Acceptance:** `pnpm -r build` clean; `pnpm -r test` exits 0 in network-blocked env (same green count as pre-change baseline); the converted test passes through the new top-level `runCli(argv, logger, { embeddings })` form; `node packages/cli/dist/bin.js --help` exits 0 (smoke-check that two-arg `runCli` still works for production). **Reference diff:** PR #40's `packages/cli/src/index.ts` portion (closed, audited by planner — +12 LOC at the right anchor points). **Evaluation Contract:** `tmp/eval-wi-ci-offline-03.json`. **Scope Manifest:** `tmp/scope-wi-ci-offline-03.json` (already pushed to runtime via `cc-policy workflow scope-sync`; allowed_paths = `index.ts`, `cli.test.ts`, `MASTER_PLAN.md`, the two `tmp/` artifacts; forbidden_paths includes every per-command file under `packages/cli/src/commands/*.ts`, every v1-wave-3 sister surface, and `bootstrap.yml`/`test.yml`/`bootstrap/expected-roots.json`). **Pre-assigned decision:** DEC-CI-OFFLINE-006 (top-level `CliOptions.embeddings` is the canonical injection seam for `runCli`; per-command options remain accepted as bounded backward compatibility but new tests SHOULD use the top-level form). Runtime: workflow_id `WI-CI-OFFLINE-03`, goal_id `g-wi-ci-offline-03`, work_item_id `wi-ci-offline-03`. | (none — fully unblocked off main at `221a957`; orthogonal to v1-wave-3 lowering chain and v2 self-hosting chain) | approve | active 2026-05-03 — planner persisted plan + eval contract + scope manifest; ready for guardian (provision) on branch `wrath/issue-43-clioptions-seam` |

Single-WI initiative; no dependency map needed. Critical path = 1 wave. When this lands, `runCli` is the canonical CLI entry for tests that need offline embedding injection, and the per-command-import bypass pattern becomes a documented bounded-backwards-compatibility seam (DEC-CI-OFFLINE-006) rather than the only way to inject.

### Initiative: WI-CI-FAST-PATH — Tiered PR CI (Phases 1 + 3: Tier-1 fast-path + nightly)

Status: **active 2026-05-10.** Issue #196. Phase 1 owned by Wrath (landed PR #234); Phase 3 owned by FuckGoblin (landed PR TBD). Runtime workflow id: `wi-ci-fast-path-phase-1`. Runtime goal id: `g-wi-ci-fast-path-phase-1`.

**Why this initiative exists.** The existing trio of CI workflows (`bootstrap.yml`, `test.yml`, `wave-3-parity.yml`) all fire on every PR and take 30–90 minutes each. This burns developer feedback loops and blocks sister-session PRs from getting CI signal in time to act on it before context compacts. Phase 1 stops the bleeding by shipping a new `.github/workflows/pr-ci.yml` that gates PRs in ≤5 min on the median PR. Phase 3 adds daily scheduled coverage so the full suite runs even on days with no pushes to main.

**Phase 1 scope (landed PR #234):**
- Add `.github/workflows/pr-ci.yml` — Tier-1 PR CI workflow (DEC-CI-FAST-PATH-PHASE-1-001..006).
- Add `scripts/affected-packages.sh` — thin affected-package base-ref resolver (DEC-CI-FAST-PATH-PHASE-1-002).
- Modify `bootstrap.yml`, `test.yml`, `wave-3-parity.yml` — drop `pull_request:` triggers; retain `push: { branches: [main] }` (DEC-CI-FAST-PATH-PHASE-1-005).
- MASTER_PLAN.md — 6 Decision Log entries + this initiative section.

**Phase 1 mechanism:** lint + typecheck run full-workspace always (cheap, turbo-cached). build + test run via `pnpm --filter "...[origin/<base-ref>]"` (affected packages + their dependents). Branch hygiene check via existing `scripts/pre-pr-check.sh`. No source files touched.

**Phase 3 scope (this WI — FuckGoblin):**
- Add `.github/workflows/nightly.yml` — Tier-2 nightly cron workflow (DEC-CI-FAST-PATH-PHASE-3-001).
- Update comments in `bootstrap.yml`, `test.yml`, `wave-3-parity.yml` to reference `nightly.yml`.
- Add CI status badges to `README.md` (Tier-1 PR CI + Nightly).
- MASTER_PLAN.md — 1 Decision Log entry + this initiative section update.

**Phase 3 mechanism:** `nightly.yml` runs on `schedule: cron: '0 3 * * *'` (03:00 UTC daily) and `workflow_dispatch`. Three jobs mirror the trio exactly (including cache-skip logic). A `notify-failure` job runs `if: always() && contains(needs.*.result, 'failure')` and creates a GitHub issue assigned to `cneckar` so no regression goes undetected.

**Explicitly deferred to follow-up WIs:**
- B6 air-gapped CI gate (blocked on #190 landing) — follow-up WI filed.
- `FAST_CHECK_NUM_RUNS` env-var reduction — requires source-side `*.props.ts` refactor; follow-up WI filed.
- Vitest fork cap (`poolOptions.forks.maxForks`) — DEC-INFRA-VITEST-FORK-CAP-001 is not backed by current vitest configs; follow-up WI filed.
- Phase 2 (test selection improvements beyond affected-package detection) — addressed by Phase 1's `scripts/affected-packages.sh`; no separate WI needed.
- Release CI (cross-platform, manual trigger, full benchmarks) — separate WI when release cadence is established.

### Initiative: Shave-what-shaves + glue framing (WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE)

Status: **active 2026-05-04.** Operator decision 2026-05-04 — architectural reframing, planning only. Implementation tickets filed post-merge.

This initiative documents the shift from **strict-subset-or-fail** to **shave-what-shaves + glue**. The slicer becomes a search algorithm (find maximal shaveable subgraphs, emit `GlueLeafEntry` for the rest) rather than a gate (whole-file must fit strict-subset or it is rejected). The IR strict-subset rules survive unchanged as the **predicate** applied per-subgraph; what changes is the scope of application — per-subgraph rather than per-file.

**Three triplet variants under the new framing:**
- `local` — shaveable, content-addressed, in the registry (existing)
- `foreign` — external dep, opaque leaf (existing, landed via WI-V2-04)
- `glue` — project-specific code that doesn't fit any strict subset; preserved verbatim in the project's source tree, NOT stored in the registry, but tracked in the slice plan so the compile pipeline knows where the boundary is (NEW — see follow-up WI-V2-GLUE-LEAF-CONTRACT)

**Tool-reuse principle for language frontends (DEC-V2-FRONTEND-TOOL-REUSE-001):** For any new source language, yakcc reuses mature upstream parsers (tree-sitter-* family), type-checkers (mypy, pyright, rust-analyzer, clangd), and transpilers rather than reimplementing them. Coverage gaps in the upstream tool become glue boundaries, not blocking failures. The TS frontend (ts-morph wrapping the TypeScript compiler) is the canonical example. See also "Long-term: multi-language shave" below.

**Scope compression from this reframing:**
- v2 self-shave PoC (WI-V2-08/09/10): ~30-40% timeline compression; failures become glue rather than fixup-loops back to refactor work.
- Multi-language story: total effort for new-language frontends drops ~50% (11-19 weeks vs 21-43 weeks for strict-subset Python as canonical example).
- Self-hosted dep migration: 5-8 weeks vs 8-12 weeks (harvest shaveable TS atoms, let glue boundary cover the rest).

| ID | Title | Description | Deps | Gate | State |
|----|-------|-------------|------|------|-------|
| WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE | Architectural reframing: shave-what-shaves + glue (#78) | Planning-only. Deliver: MASTER_PLAN.md initiative section + Decision Log entries (DEC-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE-001, DEC-V2-FRONTEND-TOOL-REUSE-001) + WI-V2-08/09/10 scope annotations + multi-language section update + audit document at `tmp/wi-v2-glue-aware-shave-audit.md` + 5 follow-up implementation tickets. No source changes. | none | approve | landed 2026-05-04 — FuckGoblin (claude-sonnet-4-6) |
| WI-V2-GLUE-LEAF-CONTRACT | Add GlueLeafEntry to SlicePlan union + compile pipeline consumer (#95) | (a) `GlueLeafEntry` type exported from `@yakcc/shave` (kind:"glue", source, canonicalAstHash, reason). (b) `SlicePlanEntry` union extended; `SlicePlan.sourceBytesByKind` gains `glue` bucket. (c) `compileToTypeScript(plan)` in `@yakcc/compile` emits glue verbatim with comment boundaries (DEC-V2-GLUE-LEAF-TS-EMIT-001). (d) `assertNoGlueLeaf(plan)` + `GlueLeafInWasmModeError` reject glue in WASM mode (DEC-V2-GLUE-LEAF-WASM-001 option a). (e) `shave()` skips GlueLeafEntry in ShavedAtomStub construction. Tests: JSON round-trip, sourceBytesByKind.glue=0 baseline, mixed-plan fixture, all compile pipeline tests. | WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE | approve | landed 2026-05-04 — FuckGoblin (claude-sonnet-4-6) |
| WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-IMPL | Full glue-aware shave implementation — 5 layers, subsumes #96–#99 + #57 + #68 (#95) | L1: GlueLeafEntry contract (landed PR #104). L2: slicer search algorithm — `SliceOptions.shaveMode`, `walkNodeGlueAware()` using `validateStrictSubset` per-subgraph. L3: compile pipeline consumer — `compileToTypeScript` emits glue verbatim with comment boundaries; `assertNoGlueLeaf` + `GlueLeafInWasmModeError` for WASM mode (landed PR #104). L4: wave-3 lowering glue integration — two `LoweringError("unsupported-node")` guards in visitor.ts: (a) record string field equality (#68 LOWER-06) cannot safely lower via pointer comparison; (b) cross-domain comparison (#57 LOWER-03) between bigint i64 and number i32 produces invalid WASM type mismatch. Both annotated `@decision DEC-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE-001`. Tests added in records.test.ts (record-06) and bigint.test.ts (LOWER-03). L5: V2 PoC re-spec audit at `tmp/wi-v2-glue-aware-impl-audit.md`. | WI-V2-GLUE-LEAF-CONTRACT | approve | landed 2026-05-04 — FuckGoblin (claude-sonnet-4-6) |

**Follow-up implementation tickets (filed post-merge — NOT in scope for WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE):**
1. **WI-V2-GLUE-LEAF-CONTRACT** — Add `GlueLeafEntry` to the SlicePlan union; extend registry schema (glue not stored in registry); update compile pipeline's slice-plan consumer. **→ landed 2026-05-04**
2. **WI-V2-SLICER-SEARCH-ALG** — Rewrite slicer from "recurse-and-throw-on-unknown" to "find-maximal-shaveable-subgraphs." Unblocked by WI-V2-GLUE-LEAF-CONTRACT. **→ landed 2026-05-04 (L2 of WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-IMPL)**
3. **WI-V2-COMPILE-GLUE-AWARE** — Extend `compileToTypeScript` and `compileToWasm` to handle GlueLeaf references at block-resolution granularity. **→ landed 2026-05-04 (L3 of WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-IMPL)**
4. **WI-V2-WAVE-3-LOWERING-GLUE-INTEGRATION** — Adjust wave-3 slices' `LoweringError` paths to emit `GlueLeaf` rather than throw, where appropriate. **→ landed 2026-05-04 (L4 of WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-IMPL): LOWER-06 + LOWER-03 guards in visitor.ts**
5. **WI-V2-PoC-COMPRESSION-AUDIT** — Re-spec remaining PoC slices (WI-V2-08/09/10) under the new framing with revised acceptance criteria. **→ landed 2026-05-04 (L5 of WI-V2-GLUE-AWARE-IMPL): see tmp/wi-v2-glue-aware-impl-audit.md**

### Long-term: multi-language shave

Status: **vision (no active work).** Operator decision 2026-05-03.

Yakcc's content-addressed registry identifies blocks by canonical AST hash. The TypeScript IR strict-subset is the first language target; the architecture is intentionally not TS-locked. Future versions extend the shave pipeline to Rust, C++, Python, and other languages whose source can be canonicalized to a normal form and lowered to WASM (or a future common substrate). The registry schema treats source language as opaque metadata: two blocks with byte-identical canonical-form bytes share an identity regardless of their source language, by construction (DEC-IDENTITY-005).

**Architectural commitments downstream of this vision:**

- The block schema MUST extend cleanly to discriminate by source language without breaking existing rows. The current `kind: 'local' | 'foreign'` discriminator (DEC-V2-FOREIGN-BLOCK-SCHEMA-001) is the first step; future versions may carry `sourceLanguage: 'ts' | 'rust' | ...` as a separate column without changing `block_merkle_root` for existing TS blocks.
- The WASM host contract is the SHARED syscall boundary across all languages. A Rust-shaved block and a TS-shaved block both call `host_fs_read` the same way. The host contract is therefore a load-bearing project-wide artifact, not a TS-implementation detail. See WI-WASM-HOST-CONTRACT-V2 (#54) for the v2 surface.
- The IR strict-subset notion generalizes: every supported language has its own strict-subset and validator. The contract is "what can yakcc safely shave?" — TypeScript's answer is the v0 IR; Rust's answer is whatever subset of safe Rust the registry can canonicalize.
- **Tool-reuse is non-negotiable for new language frontends (DEC-V2-FRONTEND-TOOL-REUSE-001, 2026-05-04).** For any new source language, yakcc reuses mature upstream parsers (tree-sitter-* family — pure WASM, no language runtime needed), type-checkers (mypy, pyright, rust-analyzer, clangd — consulted at shave-time as foreign tools), and transpilers as starting points rather than reimplementing them from scratch. Coverage gaps in the upstream tool become **glue boundaries** under the shave-what-shaves framing (DEC-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE-001) — they do NOT block the shave. Estimate for adding a new language drops from "21-43 weeks (strict-subset)" to "11-19 weeks (glue-aware + tool-reuse)" for a language like Python. See "Initiative: Shave-what-shaves + glue framing" above.

No tickets are open against this initiative today. Its role is to keep current decisions from foreclosing it. Any decision that would make multi-language extension a breaking change to the registry SHALL be flagged at reviewer time. See DEC-V2-FOREIGN-POLICY-PROGRESSION-001 for the related progression: every dep eventually shaved, with foreign-policy as the operator-facing knob during the transition.

### Self-hosted dependency migration plan

Status: **active planning 2026-05-03** (audit landed; per-dep implementation tickets file as the operator approves migration paths).

Yakcc currently depends on a small set of npm packages that prevent the project from achieving the operator's self-hosted vision: yakcc shaves itself, recompiles itself, runs as pure WASM. Each dep needs an explicit migration trajectory recorded here, otherwise the project drifts toward "yakcc that compiles other TS to WASM but is itself a Node app forever."

This section is the live audit. It does not commit any sister to implementation; it records intent so that downstream decisions can be evaluated against it.

**Migration path taxonomy:**

- **(A) Shave it** — vendor the TS source from upstream, slicer recurses into it. Use `--foreign-policy=reject` to enforce. The dep becomes content-addressed atoms in the registry.
- **(B) Replace it with pure-TS implementation** — narrower than upstream's full feature set, just what yakcc needs.
- **(C) Treat as host syscall boundary** — fold its surface into WASM_HOST_CONTRACT v2 (WI-WASM-HOST-CONTRACT-V2, #54) so the runtime provides it, not the WASM module.
- **(D) Drop the feature** — yakcc functionality that depends on this dep is descoped or made optional in self-hosted mode.

**Summary table:**

| Dep | Current usage | Path | Rationale | Multi-lang |
|-----|---------------|------|-----------|-----------|
| `better-sqlite3` | `packages/registry/src/storage.ts` (the entire registry storage layer) | **C now, A future** | Native C++ bindings — nothing to shave at the JS level. Treat as host capability for the PoC; eventual A path needs a multi-language shave (SQLite C source becomes a future Rust/C++ shave target). | Yes — SQLite C source is a future shave target across languages |
| `sqlite-vec` | Vector index for embedding search in `@yakcc/registry` | **D for self-hosted, C for hosted** | Native C SQLite extension. Embedding similarity is "just an index" per Cornerstone #4 — selection reads structural match + declared strictness, never cosine distance. Self-hosted yakcc can drop this and rely on structural matching alone; hosted operators who want semantic search keep it as a host capability. | Same as better-sqlite3 |
| `ts-morph` | `packages/ir/`, `packages/shave/`, `packages/compile/src/wasm-lowering/` (TS parsing + AST manipulation) | **B (longest pole)** | Largest non-shaveable surface in the project. ts-morph wraps the TypeScript compiler; both are JS that runs in any JS engine, but ts-morph itself is shaveable in principle (TS source). The replacement target is "ts-morph but narrowed to yakcc's actual needs": parse, walk, declarationKind, getTypeNode().getText() — no full type checker. Estimate: 2-4 weeks. | TS-specific — future Rust/C++ parsers won't go through ts-morph; each language has its own parser. |
| `@xenova/transformers` | `packages/contracts/src/embeddings.ts` (`createLocalEmbeddingProvider()` — network-bound) | **C or D** | ONNX runtime + transformers.js model is heavy and network-bound. `createOfflineEmbeddingProvider()` (BLAKE3 stub, shipped at `4d29b30`) already covers the deterministic offline path — bootstrap + tests run fully without this dep. For self-hosted yakcc with semantic search, fold into a `host_embedding_compute` syscall (path C); for self-hosted yakcc that drops semantic search, path D. | Embedding is language-neutral; either path applies across all source languages. |
| `@noble/hashes` | BLAKE3 throughout `@yakcc/contracts` (`canonicalAstHash`, `blockMerkleRoot`, etc.) | **A (shaveable today)** | Already pure JS, no native deps. Smallest migration in the audit — just run yakcc shave against `@noble/hashes`'s source and accept the resulting atoms into the canonical corpus. | Hashing is universal; shaving this doesn't affect future language support. |
| `node:fs`, `node:path`, `node:util`, `node:os` | Throughout — bootstrap, CLI, registry, test fixtures | **C** | Maps cleanly to `host_fs_*`, `host_proc_*`, `host_path_*` via WI-WASM-HOST-CONTRACT-V2 (#54). The WASI subset adopted there IS this dep's migration path. | Yes — the host contract is the shared syscall surface across all languages. |
| `vitest` | Test framework, dev-only | **out of scope** | Tests don't ship in the WASM yakcc bundle. Self-hosted yakcc runs without vitest at runtime; vitest stays a dev-only dep. | N/A |
| `typescript` | Build dep for tsc compilation (`pnpm -r build`) | **out of scope** | Build-time only. The shaved corpus IS the runtime artifact; once yakcc shaves itself, `pnpm -r build` is a developer convenience, not a runtime requirement. | N/A |

**Proposed migration sequence (no commitments yet — operator-approval-gated):**

1. `@noble/hashes` (path A) — smallest, lowest risk, validates that path A actually works against a real dep
2. `node:fs` etc. (path C) — gated by WI-WASM-HOST-CONTRACT-V2 (#54)
3. `@xenova/transformers` (path D for self-hosted scope; revisit C if/when semantic search returns)
4. `sqlite-vec` (path D for self-hosted; revisit C alongside better-sqlite3)
5. `better-sqlite3` (path C with eventual A) — load-bearing, deepest migration
6. `ts-morph` (path B) — longest pole, scoped to yakcc-narrow-needs replacement, not feature parity with upstream

This sequence is the **post-PoC track**. The v2 self-shave PoC (Serenity's chain through #62) explicitly does NOT depend on any of this — it ships with foreign-policy=tag and accepts every dep above as a foreign leaf. Migrations begin after PoC closure.

**Decision authority:** every dep migration lands as its own WI with an `@decision DEC-V2-DEPS-{DEP}-001` annotation recording the chosen path and rationale at the time of migration. This audit table is the live tally; rows update as paths shift or migrations land.

### Initiative: AS-backend WASM track (Phase 2 + Phase 3 retirement of hand-rolled emitter)

Status: **wave-3 lowering retired 2026-05-10 (wi-148-cleanup / #148). All four phases plus cleanup closed.** Operator-adjudicated pivot at issue #142 (closed 2026-05-06): AssemblyScript replaces the hand-rolled WASM emitter as the production WASM compilation path. Phase 0 (#144), Phase 1 (#145) + follow-up (#170), Phase 2 (#146), Phase 3 (#147), and cleanup (#148) have all landed under the parent initiative **#143**. The in-house TS→WASM lowerer (`wasm-backend.ts` + `wasm-lowering/` + `wasm-host.ts` + `WASM_HOST_CONTRACT.md`, ~8K LoC) was deleted in the cleanup pass; `assemblyscript@0.28.17` was promoted from `devDependencies` to `dependencies` in `packages/compile/package.json`. See `DEC-AS-BACKEND-PIVOT-001` for the load-bearing decision (now closed) and `DEC-V1-WASM-HOST-CONTRACT-DISPOSITION-001` for the host-contract disposition.

**Why this initiative exists.** Phase 0/1 closed via GitHub issues only — no DEC entry, no MASTER_PLAN initiative, no superseding annotation on the wave-2/wave-3 strategy decisions. A new contributor reading the plan in good faith would still believe the hand-rolled emitter is the production path. Per AGENTS.md *"Do not paper over disagreement between the plan and reality"* — this initiative closes the gap.

**Plan-state correction (2026-05-10).** During the 2026-05-10 PM review, I drafted Phase 2 / Phase 3 issues without first searching the existing backlog and filed #197 / #198 as duplicates of #146 / #147. Both have been closed as duplicates. **Use #146 / #147 / #148.** The corresponding issue audit is recorded in the Plan history milestones section.

**Current code surface (2026-05-10, post-cleanup).**
- `packages/compile/src/as-backend.ts` (408 LoC) — sole production WASM compilation path.
- `packages/compile/src/wasm-backend.ts` — **DELETED** (wave-2 hand-rolled emitter, 2,027 LoC removed).
- `packages/compile/src/wasm-lowering/` — **DELETED** (wave-3 lowering pass, 9 source files + sibling props/tests, ~5,700 LoC removed).
- `packages/compile/src/wasm-host.ts` + sibling host tests — **DELETED**; AS uses standard WASI/wasmtime host imports.

- `assemblyscript@0.28.17` — **promoted** from `devDependencies` to `dependencies` in `packages/compile/package.json`.
- Net change: ~8K LoC source + tests deleted; 45 files changed (31 deletions, 8 modifications).

### Initiative: v3 discovery (D-series implementation rollout)

Status: **design pass complete (D1..D6 ADRs landed); implementation gated on measurement check.** This initiative is the implementation-side container for the v3 stage above. The 6 ADRs landed 2026-05-08..2026-05-10 are the v3 design pass; the implementation WIs named inside those ADRs are tracked here as the live ledger. See `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001` for the operator decision opening this stage in parallel with v2 closure.

**Measurement-first guardrail (load-bearing).** Per `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002` (2026-05-10 amendment), the original measurement-first gate from `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001` cannot fire on the PR #254 / PR #267 baseline because that measurement is contaminated by (a) too-small corpus (N=5 seed-derived) and (b) the `DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002` store/query text-asymmetry violation. **Two prereqs must land before the gate fires:** `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-CORPUS-SEED` (#269 — stratified corpus on full yakcc shave registry, ~1,773+ atoms across 5 query categories) AND `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY` (#270 — symmetric query-text derivation via `findCandidatesByQuery`). Only then does re-running the D5 harness produce a clean M1 number that the operator can act on. Cornerstone #4 ("embedding is just an index") is preserved either way: D3 Stage 2 structural filter remains binary; cosine never decides correctness regardless of which path the operator chooses.

If pause: file re-spec WI; CLI/MCP run on single-vector path with the symmetric-query API from #270.

**Out of scope.** Per-dimension model selection (v3.1 trigger). PCA reduction (v3.1 trigger at 1M+ atoms). Captured-session benchmark corpus (v3.1). Federation of v3 indices (future F-axis pass). Relaxation of cornerstone #4 (embedding-as-index-only is preserved; structural match decides selection regardless of cosine).

### Initiative: WI-HOOK-LAYER (v0.5 GTM surface — local-dev usability)

Status: **active 2026-05-10.** Parent initiative at [#194](https://github.com/cneckar/yakcc/issues/194) (filed by orchestrator 2026-05-10, ~2 hours before the PM review that surfaced the v0.5 facade gap). Closes "yakcc is a registry without a consumer" by wiring the production hook (already shipped per `DEC-HOOK-CLAUDE-CODE-PROD-001`) into a real Claude Code integration surface. This is the load-bearing user-facing surface — without it, yakcc is research-grade and not locally usable.

**Why this initiative exists.** Discovered during the 2026-05-10 PM review: `yakcc hooks claude-code install` is still the v0 facade (writes `.claude/CLAUDE.md` documenting the v0 stub message); the production hook in `packages/hooks-claude-code/src/index.ts` is real but writes a marker file because "the Claude Code CLI extension API does not expose a Node.js-callable slash-command registration surface." Issue #194 is the design-pass parent. This MASTER_PLAN section is the substrate-level container so the work is visible alongside v2 / v3 / AS-track in the active initiatives ledger.

**Phase plan** (per #194 body):
- **Phase 0** — design pass (orchestrator-driven, ~1 session). Resolves D-HOOK-1 through D-HOOK-6 (first IDE target, interception layer, sync vs async, contract surfacing, telemetry shape, discovery-v3 integration shape). Output: `docs/adr/hook-layer-architecture.md`.
- **Phase 1** — telemetry-only MVP. Tool-call interception + telemetry capture, no substitution yet. Estimate: ~3 weeks once D1 (#151) lands.
- **Phase 2** — smart substitution via discovery v3 (D4 #154 lands). Estimate: ~4 weeks after Phase 1.
- **Phase 3** — contract surfacing per D-HOOK-4 (B5 prereq). Estimate: ~2 weeks after Phase 2.
- **Phase 4** — Cursor adapter (independent of benchmarks). Estimate: ~3 weeks.
- **Phase 5** — agnostic / proxy mode (conditional, only if demand surfaces).

**Sub-ticket cascade landed during the 2026-05-10 PM review** (gap-fillers not covered by #194's phase decomposition):

| ID | Title | GH Issue | State | Notes |
|----|-------|----------|-------|-------|
| Parent | WI-HOOK-LAYER (initiative) | [#194](https://github.com/cneckar/yakcc/issues/194) | active | Phase-0 design-pass parent |
| Sub | WI-V05-CLI-INSTALL-RETIRE-FACADE | [#203](https://github.com/cneckar/yakcc/issues/203) | blocked on #194 Phase 0 | Replaces the v0 facade in `packages/cli/src/commands/hooks-install.ts` with real wiring (settings.json hook / MCP server / both per #194's chosen surface). |

**Cornerstone alignment** (per #194 body — restated for the substrate-level record):
- **No ownership** preserved. Hook telemetry is hard-coded local-only by default; opt-in upload requires explicit operator config; zero personally-identifying data ever collected.
- **Content-addressed** preserved. Atom resolution returns BlockMerkleRoot hashes; the hook never invents identifiers.
- **No versioning** preserved. Hook protocol designed for additive evolution.
- **Composition from minimal blocks** preserved. Decomposed into `@yakcc/hooks-base` + `@yakcc/hooks-claude-code` + `@yakcc/hooks-cursor` + `@yakcc/hooks-codex` (per existing v0 package layout) plus the `@yakcc/cli` install-side WI #203.
- **Embedding-as-index-only** preserved. Substitution requires structural + property-test validation, never cosine alone (D-HOOK-3 + D-HOOK-4 enforce this).

**Dispatch order:** #194 Phase 0 (design ADR) first. Then #203 → #204 (CLI surface lands fast once design is locked). Phase 1 telemetry MVP can run in parallel with #203/#204. Phase 2/3/4 sequence per #194's plan. #205 (walkthrough doc) lands last, after Phase 1 ships and the install + init commands work.

**Out of scope.** Web-IDE integration (browser hosts, Replit, Codespaces) — separate initiative if demand surfaces. Non-coding agent integration (research / analysis agents) — outside GTM thesis. Multi-user / shared-team telemetry — not in v0.5 (no-ownership cornerstone preserved).

**Why this matters for "can I use yakcc for local dev":** the answer to that question lives entirely in this initiative. v0/v0.6/v0.7 / v1 / v2 / v3 are all infrastructure for the hook layer. Without WI-HOOK-LAYER closure, yakcc is a registry plus a CLI; with it, yakcc is the substrate the MANIFESTO promises.

### Initiative: WI-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCEMENT — pr-ci.yml is the merge gate (SPIKE with #294)

Status: **active 2026-05-11.** Issue [#297](https://github.com/cneckar/yakcc/issues/297). Owned by Wrath (operator-reassigned from FuckGoblin). Paired SPIKE with [#294](https://github.com/cneckar/yakcc/issues/294) — the broken-build bug whose PR serves as the natural regression test for the new merge gate. Runtime workflow id: `wi-ci-merge-gate-enforcement`. Runtime goal id: `g-wi-ci-merge-gate-enforcement`.

**Why this initiative exists.** WI-CI-FAST-PATH Phase 1 (PR #234) shipped `.github/workflows/pr-ci.yml` with the right architectural bones — lint + typecheck full-workspace, build+test affected-packages-filtered, branch hygiene check, B6a air-gap bench. But two implementation gaps let multiple Wrath PRs (#221, #271, #285, #291, #301) land broken builds on `main`: (1) `build-and-test` uses `pnpm --filter "...[origin/main]"` rather than full-workspace `pnpm -r build`, missing package-graph regressions where a downstream consumer is not in the diff but the dependency-graph evaluation differs from pnpm's affected resolution; (2) **branch protection on `main` is not enforced at all** (`gh api repos/cneckar/yakcc/branches/main/protection` returns HTTP 404 "Branch not protected" as of 2026-05-11), so a PR with red checks can be merged via the GitHub UI's force-merge button or via `gh pr merge --admin`. The five most recent pr-ci.yml runs (PRs #301, #300, #298, #295, plus open feature branches) ALL completed with `conclusion=failure` — every Wrath PR this session has merged on top of red CI by manual operator override. This is the failure pattern this WI ends mechanically.

**Operator policy this WI codifies (cited from #297 body):**

> **`pnpm -r build` success is the merge gate. Anything that takes >5 min (bootstrap shave, full test suite, wave-3 parity) is async via nightly.yml and does NOT gate merges.**

**Spike exit criteria (must hold simultaneously to close #297):**
- `pnpm -r build` succeeds from a clean clone of `main`.
- `gh api repos/cneckar/yakcc/branches/main/protection --jq '.required_status_checks.contexts'` lists at minimum `lint (full workspace)`, `typecheck (full workspace)`, `build + test (full workspace)`, `branch hygiene check` as required check names.
- A sentinel PR with a deliberately-broken build CANNOT be merged via `gh pr merge` (returns "merging is blocked: required status check has not passed").
- #294's PR has landed by going through pr-ci.yml — proving the gate works end-to-end.

**Why this is a 4-slice initiative, not single-slice.** Three irreducible orderings force decomposition:

1. **Pre-existing failures must be repaired BEFORE branch protection turns on.** Main today has broken builds (issue #294: type errors in `@yakcc/shave` and `@yakcc/compile`), broken lints (`useLiteralKeys` in `cli.test.ts` + `hooks-install.test.ts`), broken module resolution (`hooks-base` missing `@noble/hashes/utils.js`), and a failing B6a air-gap benchmark. Turning on required-status-checks on `main` while these are red would block every sister's merges. Slices A1+A2 fix pre-existing failures FIRST; Slice C enforces protection AFTER.
2. **Switching the build filter (Slice B) and configuring branch protection (Slice C) have orthogonal failure modes.** Slice B is a yaml syntax change; Slice C is a `gh api PUT` call requiring `viewerCanAdminister`. Bundling them couples a yaml-parse failure with a permissions failure during land. Separated, each can land independently.
3. **The spike-exit verification (Slice D) is itself a deliberately-broken sentinel PR — it must run AFTER protection is on, and it must be CLOSED-not-merged.** That cannot be the same PR as Slice C.

**Slice A2 is the immediate next work item** now that Slice A1 has landed (merge `e220f3e`, feature commit `931d34f`, 2026-05-11; closes #294). The orchestrator should re-engage the planner for Slice A2's Evaluation Contract + Scope Manifest.

**Acceptance per #297 (verbatim, spike-level):**
- pr-ci.yml's `build-and-test` job uses `pnpm -r build` (full workspace) — Slice B.
- Branch protection rule on `main` requires `pr-ci.yml` checks to pass before merge — Slice C.
- Verification artifact committed: `gh api repos/cneckar/yakcc/branches/main/protection --jq '.required_status_checks.checks'` output saved under `tmp/` — Slice C.
- A test PR with intentionally broken build shows GitHub's merge button is disabled — Slice D.
- AGENTS.md (CONTRIBUTING.md does not exist; AGENTS.md is the canonical authority) documents the policy — Slice C.
- #294's PR is the natural regression test — **landed via Slice A1** (merge `e220f3e`, 2026-05-11).
- MASTER_PLAN.md records `DEC-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCE-001` capturing the policy + the implementation — this initiative section + Decision Log entries below (orchestrator will append the `landed PR #N` cells per slice as they complete; per operator instruction, the implementer does NOT touch MASTER_PLAN.md).

**Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups, not built here):**
- B6a air-gap benchmark (`B6a air-gap benchmark (zero outbound)`) is NOT added to required-status-checks in Slice C. It is currently failing on every PR (legitimate B6a issues separate from this WI). Adding it as required would block merges on a separate failure mode. Follow-up WI to be filed once B6a is green.
- Auto-merge configuration is unchanged. GitHub's auto-merge respects required-status-checks by default; nothing to add.
- Cross-platform Windows/macOS runners — out of scope; release-tier per #196 Phase 3 future work.
- Test gating shape (`pnpm -r test` is currently in pr-ci.yml's affected filter) — out of scope; the merge gate is BUILD success per operator policy, not full-test success. Test step retains affected-packages filter for speed (DEC-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCE-002).
- Bootstrap-verify gating shape (`yakcc bootstrap --verify`) is async via push:main on `bootstrap.yml` — unchanged.
- Wave-3-parity gating shape (`wave-3 closer parity`) is async via push:main on `wave-3-parity.yml` — unchanged.

The merge gate's effectiveness can be exercised informally on any future PR with a deliberate type error. |

Critical path = 5 slices over 4 waves: (Slice A1) → (Slice A2) → (Slice B) → (Slice C) → (Slice D). Slice A2 is the immediate next work item now that Slice A1 has landed. Each subsequent slice triggers planner re-engagement.

**Why planner re-engages between slices.** Slices B/C/D's Evaluation Contracts depend on facts only known after the prior slice lands: Slice B needs to know whether Slice A1's fixes transitively repair some Slice A2 surface; Slice C needs the exact status-check names emitted by the modified pr-ci.yml in Slice B; Slice D needs to verify Slice C's branch-protection JSON was applied correctly. Authoring all four contracts up-front would over-specify and force re-planning.

**Cornerstone alignment**:
- **Architecture preservation.** Branch protection becomes the mechanically-enforced single authority for "can this PR merge"; the "merge anyway" pattern becomes IMPOSSIBLE without explicit operator action.
- **Single source of truth.** required-status-checks list IS the authority for merge-readiness; pr-ci.yml's job names ARE the authority for what those checks are; `gh api .../protection` IS the authority for whether protection is on.
- **Loud failure over silent fallback.** Broken-build PRs FAIL LOUDLY; the previous silent-merge-with-warning path is removed.

## Open questions

- **cognitive-stack monorepo conventions.** `initialize.txt` references
  cognitive-stack as the template for monorepo conventions, but the
  conventions document itself was not provided. The scaffold defaults to
  modern pnpm + Turborepo idioms (workspace protocol, `turbo.json` with task
  pipelines, package-local `tsconfig.json` extending a root base, ESLint flat
  config). When cognitive-stack conventions are shared, WI-001 will be
  re-aligned. Until then, treat current defaults as provisional.

## Cornerstone audit (2026-05-10 — sweep of last 30 days / 221 commits)

Pinpoint sweep across `packages/**/*.ts` and recent git log for cornerstone-violation shapes. **Result: cornerstones are intact.** Findings:

**Cornerstone #2 (no ownership) — clean.**
- `packages/registry/src/storage.test.ts` carries explicit negative tests asserting `blocks` table has no `author / author_email / signature / owner / signer` columns (DEC-NO-OWNERSHIP-011 invariant test).
- `packages/federation/src/wire.test.ts` carries negative tests asserting the wire format has no `signer / signature` fields.
- No production-code occurrences of `author_email`, `author_id`, `signer`, or `owner_*` columns or fields.

**Cornerstone #3 (content-addressed) — clean.**
- `BlockMerkleRoot` derivation is centralized in `@yakcc/contracts` per `DEC-IDENTITY-005` / `DEC-TRIPLET-IDENTITY-020` / `DEC-V1-FEDERATION-WIRE-ARTIFACTS-002`.
- Federation wire format consumes the contracts-package formula directly (no parallel helper).

**Cornerstone #4 (embedding is just an index) — clean with one note.**
- Selection logic in `packages/registry/src/select.ts` reads structural-match results and declared strictness, not cosine distance.
- **Note:** `packages/hooks-base/src/index.ts` uses `cosineDistance < threshold` as the *registry-hit suggestion* gate. This is **not** a correctness gate — `registry-hit` means "consider this block," not "this block is correct" — but the structural-match gate that v3 D3 specifies (`DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-001`) is not yet wired into the hook path. Until `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY` lands, cosine alone gates the suggestion. This is a known-temporary state, not a cornerstone violation, but worth flagging so it doesn't drift into permanence. **Action:** when WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY lands, the hook path MUST gate registry-hit on structural match before returning the candidate.

**Cornerstone #6 (monotonic registry) — clean.**
- No `DELETE FROM blocks` anywhere in production code.
- Schema migrations are atomic clean re-creates of `contract_embeddings` only (the index, not the source-of-truth `blocks` table) per `DEC-SCHEMA-MIGRATION-002`.

**Sacred Practice #12 (no parallel mechanisms) — clean (2026-05-10).**
- The hand-rolled WASM emitter (`packages/compile/src/wasm-backend.ts` + `wasm-lowering/` + `wasm-host.ts`, ~8K LoC) has been **deleted** under `WI-AS-CLEANUP-WAVE3-LOWERER` (#148, landed 2026-05-10). `as-backend.ts` is now the sole production WASM compilation path; `assemblyscript` is a first-class `dependencies` entry. The transient differential-oracle dual-mechanism authorized by `DEC-AS-BACKEND-PIVOT-001` has been retired on schedule and Sacred Practice #12 is honored in steady state.
- No parallel-mechanism violations remain in the sweep.

**No-versioning cornerstone — clean.**
- No occurrences of `semver` / `version.latest` / `breaking-change` semantics in production code. The only "version" usage is `SCHEMA_VERSION` (the registry-internal migration marker, not block-level versioning) and `package.json#version` (the npm-publish version, mechanical).

**Sweep scope.** 221 commits across last 30 days, all `packages/**/*.ts` non-test source files, plus a targeted regex sweep for known violation shapes. Test files were inspected for *negative* assertions (which are guards, not violations). This audit should run on a 30-day cadence; setting that up is a follow-up for the orchestrator.

## Plan compaction (deferred; needs explicit operator approval)

`MASTER_PLAN.md` is now ~360 KB / 1,950+ lines. It contains five distinct surfaces interleaved:
1. **Permanent record** (Original Intent, Identity, Cornerstone, Repo Conventions, Architecture, Stages, Trust/Scale Axis, Hard problems we are deferring).
2. **Live work surface** (Active Initiatives table — currently 12 initiatives).
3. **Decision Log** (107+ DEC entries).
4. **Plan history milestones** (append-only milestone log).
5. **Riskiest Assumptions** (some entries 12+ months old).

Recommendation (deferred): split into `MASTER_PLAN.md` (live state, surfaces 1+2 + a thin pointer to current decisions) + `PLAN_HISTORY.md` (closed initiatives, retired DECs, plan milestones, riskiest-assumptions archive). Reduces cognitive load on contributors; preserves audit trail.

This split is **not** done in the 2026-05-10 PM-review pass because it changes file structure and tooling that depends on `MASTER_PLAN.md` paths (e.g., `cc-policy workflow`, AGENTS.md references, sister-session prompts). It needs an explicit operator decision and a single dedicated WI to land.

## Plan history milestones

Append-only log of substrate-level milestones. Each entry names what
shipped, the SHA on `main`, and what it unblocks downstream. New entries
are added at the top; older entries are not edited.

- **2026-05-10 — Source-side `@decision` audit (PM follow-up to PR #208).** Cross-referenced 250 in-source `@decision DEC-*` annotations across `packages/**/*.ts` against the MASTER_PLAN decision-log + body-text. Findings: 28 in-source DECs were "load-bearing-shaped" (operator / Path-A/B / supersede / cornerstone language in their source rationale) AND had zero plan mention. Triage: 3 Tier-A backfills required (`DEC-HOOK-BASE-001`, `DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-MANIFEST-001`, `DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002`); 3 Tier-B foundational v0 choices backfilled (`DEC-STORAGE-LIBRARY-001`, `DEC-STORAGE-FAIL-LOUD-001`, `DEC-V2-BOOT-CLI-001`); 11 Tier-C implementer-scope (no backfill needed); 11 Tier-D zombie wave-3-lowering DECs scheduled for deletion under #148 (no backfill needed). **Process gap surfaced:** in-source `@decision` annotations are not auto-mirrored to the plan's decision log. Recommended follow-up — add a CI check (or stop-hook) that flags new in-source `@decision` DECs without matching plan rows when their rationale text contains operator/architectural language. **Audit re-run cadence: every 30 days, mechanically.** Methodology:
  ```
  grep -rEho "@decision\s+DEC-[A-Z0-9_-]+" packages/ --include="*.ts" | sort -u > /tmp/in-source.txt
  grep -oE "DEC-[A-Z0-9_-]+" MASTER_PLAN.md | sort -u > /tmp/in-plan.txt
  comm -23 /tmp/in-source.txt /tmp/in-plan.txt > /tmp/source-only.txt
  # for each, read source rationale, classify A/B/C/D, backfill A+B
  ```
