Survey artifact: `tmp/wi-v2-05-shave-survey.md`. The reframing was authorized by the user as Framing A at the planner's needs_user_decision boundary. |
| DEC-CLOSER-CONSUMER-FIX-001 | **Project-wide routing principle (operator decision 2026-05-05).** When a closer/parity-shape WI surfaces a gap between corpus shape and consumer capability, the routing default is **fix the consumer, not filter the corpus**. Filtering the corpus (or dropping the threshold) to match existing consumer capability reduces the closer's claim to a vacuous one — it hides the signal the closer was specifically designed to surface. **Established precedents:** (i) #36 wave-3 closer, Path (b) "drop threshold from 80% to 0.06%" REJECTED → Path (d) "regenerate corpus in-test via the same shave pipeline" APPROVED — closer DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-DEMO-CORPUS-LOADER-001. (ii) #125 wave-4 export-wrapper, Path 2 "filter corpus to atoms with `/export\s+function/`" REJECTED → Path 1 "synthesize export wrapper at `compileToWasm` entry" APPROVED — closer DEC-V1-WAVE-4-WASM-LOWER-EXTEND-002. **Application:** future closer/parity WIs MUST cite this DEC in their pre-assigned-decision section and document why their chosen path is "fix the consumer" (or, in genuinely-exceptional cases, why the corpus filter is the correct call with explicit operator approval). Examples of "fix the consumer": adding a wrapper-synthesis step at the consumer's entry point; extending the consumer's capability to handle a previously-unsupported construct; emitting a stub via the glue-aware framing (DEC-V2-GLUE-AWARE-SHAVE-001). Examples of disallowed corpus filters: dropping atoms below an arbitrary threshold; requiring the corpus to satisfy syntactic predicates the consumer happens to want; redefining "the corpus" to exclude shapes the consumer doesn't yet handle. | Operator-authorized 2026-05-05. Routing observation across #36/#120/#125. The principle is descriptive (this is what we already do) and prescriptive (this is what future closer/parity WIs SHOULD do). Reviewer authority to challenge a corpus-filter resolution that doesn't have explicit operator sign-off. |
| DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D1-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D1 (#151, 2026-05-08).** Multi-dimensional embedding schema lands as 5 vectors per atom — `embedding_behavior`, `embedding_guarantees`, `embedding_error_conditions`, `embedding_non_functional`, `embedding_property_tests` — using the existing `Xenova/all-MiniLM-L6-v2` model (DEC-EMBED-010), generated auto-from-IntentCard at atom-time with opt-in LLM-derived enrichment as a secondary pass. Stored as multi-column `sqlite-vec` `vec0` (one `FLOAT[384]` column per dimension, keyed on `spec_hash TEXT PRIMARY KEY`). 384-dim per dimension × 5 = 1,920 floats per atom (~7.68 KB/atom; ~13.6 MB at 1,773 atoms today). `signature` (`inputs`/`outputs`) stays structural — type-unification at query time, NOT embedded. Absent-dimension fallback: zero vector (query-time must skip zero-vector dimensions in similarity scoring). `preconditions` + `postconditions` + `invariants` fold into `embedding_guarantees` for v1. Migration 7 (D6's WI) must be a clean re-create (`vec0` does NOT support `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN`): drop + recreate + lazy-repopulate, mirroring migration 2's pattern. **Deferral: orthogonal to DEC-VERIFY-010** (L1+ behavioral embedding via sandbox execution); D1 owns the L0 textual schema only; DEC-VERIFY-010 columns may be added to migration 7 as additive `FLOAT[384]` columns without architectural change. v3.1 triggers: per-dimension models if D5 recall metrics surface a gap; multi-row storage if dimension count exceeds ~10; PCA reduction at 1M+ atoms; sixth assertions vector if D5 surfaces a query category requiring it. ADR: `docs/adr/discovery-multi-dim-embeddings.md`. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D1 (#151). The current single-vector embedding (DEC-EMBED-010) embeds the whole canonicalized SpecYak as one string, which loses the ability to weight dimensions at query time. The multi-dim schema makes "find atoms with this BEHAVIOR" and "find atoms with these GUARANTEES" produce distinguishably different query vectors. Multi-column `vec0` keeps the existing `spec_hash` PK semantics (two blocks sharing a spec share embeddings) and is faster query-time than multi-row at the v3 dimension count. Same model across dimensions keeps the offline-provider extension trivial (per-dimension BLAKE3 streams) and avoids new download surface. Implementation, migration 7, and the auto+LLM composition rule land in subsequent v3 implementation/migration WIs; D1 ships the design only. |
| DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D2-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D2 (#152, 2026-05-08).** Query language / API surface for the v3 discovery system. Separate `QueryIntentCard` schema (LLM-facing, freeform `string[]` for guarantees/errorConditions/propertyTests instead of storage's structured types; `Partial<NonFunctionalProperties>` allowing missing `purity`/`threadSafety`; `signature` as `{ name?, type }[]`; `weights` keyed on the 5 D1 dimension names; `topK` default 10; optional `minScore`). Query-time per-dimension presence rule mirrors D1's zero-vector skip. Zero-vector stored dimensions score as `null` (excluded from weighted sum, not `0`). **CLI: extend existing `yakcc query`** (DEC-CLI-QUERY-001) with per-dimension flags + per-dimension weight flags + `--query=path/to/query.json` + `--format=json` + `--min-score` + `--auto-accept`; free-text positional keeps current behavior-only semantics for backward compatibility. New `yakcc resolve` rejected (third near-synonym verb). **Programmatic API: `Registry.findCandidatesByQuery(query, options)`** in `@yakcc/registry` (alongside the existing `findCandidatesByIntent`). `Candidate extends CandidateMatch` adds `perDimensionScores` and `combinedScore`. New `@yakcc/discovery` package rejected for v3 (no demonstrated circularity; cite DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-004). WASM `host_resolve` and HTTP `POST /resolve` deferred to v3.1. **Iteration protocol: stateless** — each query independent; LLM owns refinement state. **Confidence: auto-accept top-1 if `combinedScore > 0.85` AND gap-to-top-2 > 0.15**, otherwise surface candidates; thresholds tunable per-query via `--auto-accept`; revisited from D5 quality data. **Cross-provider rejection invariant:** registry-time embedding provider must equal query-time provider; query planner MUST detect and reject mismatch before running KNN (cite DEC-EMBED-010, DEC-CI-OFFLINE-001). ADR: `docs/adr/discovery-query-language.md`. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D2 (#152). The query schema must be smaller than the storage `SpecYak` (LLM-facing surface; freeform descriptions instead of structured ids+errorTypes), and explicit weights are required because D1's 5-vector schema has no implicit weighting. Extending `yakcc query` rather than adding `yakcc resolve` keeps the CLI verb count flat (already 2 near-synonyms: `search` for structural, `query` for vector). Keeping the new method in `@yakcc/registry` matches `findCandidatesByIntent` placement (DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-001) and avoids the shave→registry circular-dep risk that DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-004 already navigates. Stateless iteration is simpler and removes a server-state dependency; the LLM already holds context. The 0.85 / 0.15 threshold pair matches #152's recommendation; D5's measurement methodology will surface whether it should be tightened. Implementation lands in `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY` / `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-CLI` (named by D1's Implementation phase boundary). |
| DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D3 (#153, 2026-05-08).** Ranking + scoring algorithm for the v3 discovery system. Weighted cosine over per-dimension embeddings (renormalized over the surviving non-null dimension set; default weight 1.0; `similarity[d] = 1 - cosineDistance[d] / 2`), 5-stage pipeline (Stage 1 vector KNN, Stage 2 structural filter, Stage 3 strictness filter, Stage 4 reserved no-op for v3.1, Stage 5 final ranking + tiebreaker), tiebreaker hierarchy (property-test depth → usage history → test history → atom age → lex BlockMerkleRoot; ε = 0.02), and near-miss surface (`CandidateNearMiss extends Candidate` with `failedAtLayer: 'structural' | 'strictness' | 'property_test' | 'min_score'`). `structuralScore` is NOT folded into `combinedScore` (gated as binary Stage 2 filter). RRF rejected for v1 with worked example; D5 trigger documented. ADR: `docs/adr/discovery-ranking.md`. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D3 (#153). Weighted cosine renormalized over surviving dimensions keeps `combinedScore` in [0,1] with clear semantic bands (≥0.85 strong, 0.70–0.85 confident, 0.50–0.70 weak, <0.50 poor) regardless of how many dimensions a given atom has populated. RRF is distribution-agnostic but cannot correctly separate candidates when the caller applies unequal weights (worked example in Q2). Structural matching is a binary requirement, not a preference — folding it into the score would allow structurally-mismatched atoms to appear as "strong" candidates. Stage 4 slot is reserved now so stage numbering is stable when DEC-VERIFY-010 lands. Implementation lands in `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY`. |
| DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D4-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D4 (#154, 2026-05-10).** LLM-facing interaction design for the v3 discovery system. Single `yakcc_resolve(query: QueryIntentCard) → QueryResult` tool only in v1 (multi-step deferred to v3.1 with named trigger); fixed evidence-projection template per candidate (~80 tokens, field order locked: address → behavior → signature → score → guarantees → tests → usage); 4-band protocol (strong+auto-accept, strong+ambiguous, confident, weak) with explicit `status: "matched" | "weak_only" | "no_match"` envelope field and prescribed no-match reactions (widen-and-retry or NEW_ATOM_PROPOSAL); verbatim system-prompt text locked at `docs/system-prompts/yakcc-discovery.md` with this ADR as authority; caller-side `ConfidenceMode` enum (`"auto_accept" | "always_show" | "hybrid"` default, 0.92 stricter hybrid threshold); three pinned failure-mode shapes (`RegistryUnreachable`, `disambiguation_hint` on F2 vague-intent, `tiebreaker_reason` on F3 tied candidates); D5 boundary table (D4 pins interaction shape, D5 tunes calibration knobs). ADR: `docs/adr/discovery-llm-interaction.md`. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D4 (#154). The single-tool design avoids doubling LLM prompt surface for unmeasured benefit; D5 provides the empirical trigger for multi-step. The explicit `no_match` signal is required because silent fall-through to code-writing makes the registry invisible to the user when the registry has a real gap, defeating the registry's coverage-improvement feedback loop. `ConfidenceMode` is caller-driven (not registry-derived) because risk context lives in the LLM's prompt, not the query. The D4/D5 boundary (interaction shape vs calibration knobs) ensures a stable measurement target exists before D5 measures against it. Implementation lands in `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY` (envelope shape), `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-CLI` (human-readable rendering), and a TBD MCP tool surface WI. |
| DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5 (#155, 2026-05-10).** Quality measurement methodology for the v3 discovery system. 5 metrics locked (M1 hit-rate ≥ 80% with threshold = D3's 0.50 weak-band entry; M2 precision@1 ≥ 70% via top-1 `BlockMerkleRoot` hash equality; M3 recall@10 ≥ 90%; M4 MRR ≥ 0.7; M5 per-band Brier < 0.10 each, band midpoints 0.925/0.775/0.60/0.25). Corpus: (1) seed-derived + (2) synthetic tasks for v3.0 under `packages/registry/test/discovery-benchmark/`; captured-sessions deferred to v3.1. `BenchmarkEntry`/`BenchmarkFile`/`PendingEntry` schemas locked; corpus data owned by follow-up `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-CORPUS-SEED`. Evaluation harness: `packages/registry/src/discovery-eval.test.ts` (vitest, colocated); helpers in `discovery-eval-helpers.ts`; owned by `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-HARNESS`. Calibration: per-band Brier (P_b vs band midpoint)² feeding M5; reliability-diagram artifact in `tmp/discovery-eval/reliability-{source}.json` (.gitignored). Pending log: `packages/registry/test/discovery-benchmark/pending.json` committed in-tree (mirrors closer-parity precedent); retired entries kept as audit trail. Dual-gate CI: regression gate (new `pending.json` entries on PR diff) + absolute-threshold gate (vitest expect failures); CI YAML wiring deferred to `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-CI-GATE`. D3 calibration knob feedback loop: 5 knobs (auto-accept 0.85, hybrid 0.92, ε=0.02, K' multiplier, score band boundaries) each with measurement trigger; 5-step amendment process (measure → file revision WI → planner adjudicate → land amendment + retire pending → audit trail); cross-authority: D2 owns auto-accept gate, D4 owns hybrid threshold. ADR: `docs/adr/discovery-quality-measurement.md`. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5 (#155). D5 is the measurement contract that makes D3/D4's calibration knobs empirically revisable. Per-band Brier (not global Brier) is required because D3 explicitly bands the score and miscalibration in the "strong" band (false auto-accept) has different operational consequences than miscalibration in the "weak" band (false candidate surfaced). Committed in-tree `pending.json` follows the `pending-atoms.json` precedent — the gap log must survive reboots and contributor handoffs and must be visible in PR diffs. The corpus authoring is split to `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-CORPUS-SEED` (schema-without-data is the correct shape for a methodology ADR). The harness location (`packages/registry/src/`) follows the existing colocation convention; a new `@yakcc/discovery-eval` package is rejected on the same circular-dep grounds as D2's `@yakcc/discovery` rejection (`DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-004`). CI wiring is deferred to `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-CI-GATE` per architecture-preservation: D5 publishes the gate contract; CI adapts. |
| DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D6-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D6 (#156, 2026-05-10).** Migration and index-population strategy for the v3 discovery system. Atomic clean re-create (v6 → v7) via the existing `applyMigrations` framework (`packages/registry/src/schema.ts` line 550): bump `SCHEMA_VERSION` 6 → 7, add `MIGRATION_7_DDL` (DROP + recreate `contract_embeddings` as 5-column vec0), add `if (currentVersion < 7)` block. Two-phase migration-3 pattern: DDL in `schema.ts` (no business-logic import); repopulation + version bump in `storage.ts openRegistry` (calls `generateMultiDimEmbedding` from `@yakcc/contracts`). Schema versioning via existing `schema_version` table — no new column on `contract_embeddings`, no `schema_metadata` table. Serial re-embedding via warm `EmbeddingProvider.embed(text)` singleton (no batch API; `DEC-EMBED-010`, `DEC-EMBED-SINGLETON-CLOSURE-001`); ~50ms/atom × N; CI uses offline provider (`DEC-CI-OFFLINE-001`). Idempotency: pre-condition gate (`currentVersion < 7`) + per-`spec_hash` skip (non-NULL `embedding_behavior` row) + `sqlite_master` DDL introspection for crash recovery (skip drop+recreate if table already at v7 shape) + wrapping `db.transaction()`. No `migration_progress` table. Three block-on-failure verification gates before version bump: G1 (schema shape via `sqlite_master`), G2 (cardinality `COUNT(DISTINCT spec_hash) blocks == COUNT(*) embeddings`), G3 (KNN canary against `embedding_behavior`). Old `embedding FLOAT[384]` column NOT preserved (D1 chose clean drop). Future-migration protocol: codify existing `MIGRATION_N_DDL` + `if (currentVersion < N)` pattern; reject file-per-migration directory; 9-step normative checklist (bump constant, add DDL const, sequential block, two-phase if backfill, idempotency strategy, vitest unit coverage, decision-log entry). New implementation WI named: `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-MIGRATION-VERIFY` (implements `MigrationVerificationError` + G1/G2/G3 as standalone testable functions). Re-evaluation triggers: incremental migration at >10K atoms + >5s open latency; batch embedding at >10K atoms + >10min wall-clock; file-per-migration at >15 migrations. ADR: `docs/adr/discovery-migration.md`. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D6 (#156). Atomic clean re-create is required because `vec0` does NOT support `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN` (D1 established this). The existing `applyMigrations` framework is the canonical migration authority — a parallel `migrations/` directory would violate Architecture Preservation (single source of truth, Sacred Practice #12). Two-phase pattern follows migration 3's precedent: `schema.ts` is pure DDL with no `@yakcc/contracts` import; the backfill that calls `generateMultiDimEmbedding` belongs in `storage.ts`. Block-on-failure gates follow Architecture Preservation ("loud failure over silent fallback") — a silently-corrupted registry produces wrong query results permanently, worse than a noisy abort. D6's G2/G3 verification gates produce the structural queryability signal that D5's M1 hit-rate measurement (`DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-001`) then validates at the semantic level. Cross-references: `DEC-SCHEMA-MIGRATION-002` (clean-re-create precedent from migration 2), `DEC-STORAGE-IDEMPOTENT-001` (DELETE+INSERT pattern reused by repopulation walk), `DEC-EMBED-010` (provider interface), `DEC-CI-OFFLINE-001` (offline gate for CI). |
| DEC-AS-BACKEND-PIVOT-001 | **2026-05-10 — operator decision, closes plan/code drift on the WASM track.** AssemblyScript (`packages/compile/src/as-backend.ts`, via `assemblyscript@0.28.17`) is the production WASM compilation path. The hand-rolled emitter at `packages/compile/src/wasm-backend.ts` + `wasm-lowering/visitor.ts` (~7,700 LoC) is retained **temporarily** as a differential oracle. **Phase plan:** Phase 0 (#144, closed) discovery spike — GO. Phase 2 (`WI-AS-PHASE-2`) — coverage expansion: every IR-strict-subset construct that the hand-rolled visitor lowers must lower equivalently through `assemblyScriptBackend()`, parity-tested against the existing differential oracle. Phase 3 (`WI-AS-PHASE-3`) — retirement: delete `wasm-backend.ts` and `wasm-lowering/`, promote `assemblyscript` from devDependencies to dependencies, simplify `assemble.ts` dispatch, update `WASM_HOST_CONTRACT.md`. **This DEC supersedes `DEC-V1-WAVE-3-WASM-STRATEGY-001`** and partially supersedes `DEC-V1-WAVE-2-WASM-STRATEGY-001` (the wave-2 emitter remains as oracle through Phase 2; `WASM_HOST_CONTRACT.md` and the wave-2 type-lowering matrix carry over as the AS-track's regression baseline). Deleted `wasm-backend.ts`, `wasm-lowering/`, `wasm-host.ts`, and `WASM_HOST_CONTRACT.md`; `assemblyscript` promoted to `dependencies`. See `DEC-V1-WASM-HOST-CONTRACT-DISPOSITION-001` for the host-contract disposition.** | Source: operator adjudication on issue #142 (2026-05-06). The hand-rolled wave-3 lowering pass was discovered to be chasing an impossible target — covering the full IR-strict-subset accept set as a hand-rolled emitter would have required substantially more LoC than already shifted without a clear convergence signal, while `asc` (the AssemblyScript compiler) already covers the majority of the surface for free. The pivot was not recorded in the decision log when it happened (closed-issue thread only, plus an in-source DEC); this DEC closes the documentation gap surfaced in the 2026-05-10 PM review. Sacred Practice #12 (no parallel mechanisms) is honored over time, not in steady state: the hand-rolled emitter exists in steady state today **only because Phase 2 has not run yet**; once Phase 2 lands, Phase 3 deletes it. The differential-oracle role is bounded by Phase 2 acceptance — this is not a permanent dual-backend design. |
| DEC-V1-WASM-HOST-CONTRACT-DISPOSITION-001 | **2026-05-10 — option (b): delete.** `wasm-host.ts` and `WASM_HOST_CONTRACT.md` retired in `WI-AS-CLEANUP-WAVE3-LOWERER` (#148). AS uses standard WASI/wasmtime host imports; the in-house host contract described interfaces for the now-deleted hand-rolled emitter only. | DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX (issue #258, 2026-05-10).** M1 hit-rate threshold **amended from 0.50 to 0.40** for the bootstrap-inline baseline. PR #254 surfaced M1=0% with M2=80%/M3=100%/M4=0.85 passing — an obvious calibration bug. Empirical investigation (`tmp/discovery-eval/calibration-investigation.md`, HEAD 31192ca, local Xenova/all-MiniLM-L6-v2) showed all correct top-1 hits on seed-derived corpus produce cosineDistance in [1.02, 1.16] → combinedScore in [0.42, 0.49]; none reach 0.50. **Root cause:** `storeBlock` embeds `canonicalizeText(spec)` (full canonical JSON) while `findCandidatesByIntent` embeds `behavior + "\n" + params` — a store/query text asymmetry that pushes all cosine distances above 1.0 even for correct matches. The formula `1 - d/2` is geometrically correct; only the D5 evaluation threshold was wrong. **Path (b) accepted:** Lower threshold to 0.40 (matches empirical distribution); Path (a) rejected (changing D3 formula breaks future callers when text symmetry is fixed). Post-calibration: M1=80% PASS / M2=80% PASS / M3=100% PASS / M4=0.85 PASS / M5 poor=0.038 PASS on seed-derived corpus. **Operator decision per DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001:** M1 seed-derived = 80% PASSES the gate — v3-implementation SHOULD PAUSE pending re-spec of D1's 5-vector schema. Also fixes: M5 scope bug (#255 — M5 live test now uses full corpus matching JSON artifact); helpers unit test coverage (#256 — `discovery-eval-helpers.test.ts` ships 60+ pure metric tests per D5 ADR Q3). The text asymmetry root cause is deferred to `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY` (DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002). After that WI ships, re-calibrate M1_HIT_THRESHOLD (likely back to 0.50+). Canonical constant: `M1_HIT_THRESHOLD` in `packages/registry/src/discovery-eval-helpers.ts`. ADR amendments: D5 Q1 section + D3 When-to-revisit section. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX implementer investigation. The D5 evaluation harness had never been run against a semantic embedding provider before PR #254. When it was, M1=0% surfaced the calibration gap between the threshold (set theoretically from D3's band boundary) and the actual empirical distribution. This DEC records the threshold amendment as a calibration knob adjustment (D5 ADR Q7 process), NOT a formula change; `1 - d/2` unchanged. Issues closed: #258 (calibration fix), #255 (M5 scope), #256 (helpers unit tests). |
| DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001 | **2026-05-10 — operator decision, closes plan/code drift on the v3 discovery track.** Open a v3 substrate stage and matching active-initiative ledger row to govern the discovery-subsystem expansion that was, until now, ADR-only (D1..D6 landed 2026-05-08..2026-05-10 without a stage-level container). v3's thesis: the v0.5 hook quality bar requires query-time dimension weighting — "find atoms with this BEHAVIOR" must produce a distinguishably different query vector from "find atoms with these GUARANTEES" — and the existing single-vector embedding (DEC-EMBED-010) collapses both into one cosine. The v3 design pass is complete (D1 multi-dim schema, D2 query-language, D3 ranking, D4 LLM-interaction, D5 quality-measurement, D6 migration); the implementation pass (`WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-*`) is gated on a measurement check (see below). **Parallel-track legitimacy:** v3 runs in parallel with v2 self-hosting closure. The v2 critical path (WI-V2-07 functionally landed at WI-038/`4767b7a`; remaining: WI-V2-08/09/10) is unaffected by v3 work — the discovery subsystem touches `@yakcc/registry` and `@yakcc/contracts`'s embedding surface, not the shave/compile/bootstrap path that v2 closure exercises. The same sister cannot work on both tracks at once, but the project can. **Measurement-first guardrail:** D5's evaluation harness (`WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-HARNESS`) must run against the **existing single-vector embedding** before D6's migration 7 lands. If single-vector M1 hit-rate already meets the ≥80% target, the 5× storage cost (1,920 floats/atom vs 384) is unjustified and v3 implementation pauses pending a re-spec. Cornerstone #4 ("embedding is just an index") is preserved either way: D3's Stage 2 structural filter remains binary; cosine never decides correctness. | Source: documentation gap surfaced in 2026-05-10 PM review. The D-series ADRs are individually well-justified, but the absence of a stage-level container made it impossible for a new contributor to read MASTER_PLAN and understand "is yakcc still in v2, or has it pivoted to v3?" The answer is "both, in parallel" — and that needs to be a recorded operator decision, not an emergent property of the merge log. The measurement-first guardrail is added because D1 commits to a 5× embedding-storage increase before D5's methodology has produced any measurement against the simpler path; running the harness against the v0 single-vector embedding first is cheap and produces the empirical justification the PM review flagged as missing. |

| DEC-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCE-002 | **WI-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCEMENT (#297, 2026-05-11).** pr-ci.yml's `build-and-test` job uses `pnpm -r build` (full workspace) for the BUILD step and retains `pnpm $FILTER test` (affected packages, via `scripts/affected-packages.sh`) for the TEST step. The job's display name changes from `build + test (affected packages)` to `build + test (full workspace)` so the status-check name in branch protection accurately reflects the gate. | Build correctness and test cadence have orthogonal cost/benefit profiles. Build is fast on a 13-package monorepo with turbo cache (1-2 min full workspace), and missing a downstream package's build break is a high-severity correctness gap — especially when the regression is across the dependency graph in a way pnpm's `--filter "...[ref]"` resolution does not capture (see #294: shave + compile broke without being in any single PR's diff, because the type errors were in test files and the affected-packages logic chose to include them via dependents but the upstream type evolution wasn't flagged at PR-time on the originating PRs). Test execution has very different cost profile (vitest spinup, fast-check numRuns × N properties × per-package suite) and full-workspace test-on-every-PR was the original WI-CI-FAST-PATH motivation for the affected filter. Keeping the filter on tests preserves Phase 1's developer-feedback win; switching the build off the filter closes the correctness gap. The display-name rename is load-bearing: branch protection's required-status-checks list is keyed on the exact job name string, so the configured contexts in DEC-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCE-004 must match what the workflow emits. Renaming makes the truth visible in the GitHub UI and prevents future drift where a WI bumps the filter without updating protection. **AMENDED 2026-05-11 per Slice B / #320 (operator-stated policy clarification 'tests that take this fucking long sure as fuck shouldn\'t be critical path for merges'):** the test step is NO LONGER in the gating job. `build-and-test` was split into TWO jobs: `build (full workspace)` (GATING; `pnpm -r build`) and `test (affected packages, advisory)` (NON-GATING via `continue-on-error: true` at job level; affected-packages filter retained). Branch protection contexts now reference `build (full workspace)` — NOT the combined `build + test (full workspace)` originally specified in this DEC. The advisory job runs but does NOT block merge per DEC-001's spirit. |
| DEC-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCE-003 | **WI-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCEMENT Slice A1 (#297 / #294, 2026-05-11).** Branded-type fast-check fixture pattern: when a property-test arbitrary needs to construct a value of a branded type (e.g., `BlockMerkleRoot`, `CanonicalAstHash` in `@yakcc/compile`'s `slice-plan.props.ts`), the fixture coerces the fast-check primitive output through a NAMED brand-application helper. Preferred path: an existing exported helper from `@yakcc/contracts` or `@yakcc/compile` (single canonical authority — Sacred Practice #12). Acceptable fallback: a single named local helper (`asBlockMerkleRoot`, `asCanonicalAstHash`) defined inline in the .props.ts file using the standard `as unknown as <Brand>` pattern. REJECTED: a new exported brand-helper module (would spawn a parallel mechanism for branded-type construction); rejected: bare `as unknown as <Brand>` cast inline in every fixture (forks the brand-application surface across the test corpus). | The two patterns commonly used in TS fast-check fixtures for branded types are (a) inline `as unknown as <Brand>` casts at every construction site (forks the surface), and (b) a single named application helper. (b) is the canonical pattern across the yakcc test corpus already (see existing branded-type test fixtures in `packages/registry`, `packages/contracts` — implementer to discover and prefer the existing helper if found). Codifying the pattern as a decision prevents Slice A1's implementer from inventing pattern (a) and prevents future shave-corpus authors (Serenity / FG when they extend the property-test corpus per WI-V2-06 follow-ups) from drifting to ad-hoc casts. | DEC-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCE-004 | **WI-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCEMENT Slice C (#297, 2026-05-11).** Branch protection on `main` is configured with `enforce_admins=false`, retaining the operator's `gh pr merge --admin` override path for emergency landings (e.g., a WI-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCE-itself failure mode where the gate gets stuck on a workflow-syntax bug). `required_pull_request_reviews=null` (no human review required; the reviewer agent is the canonical technical-readiness authority per the canonical chain in CLAUDE.md). `allow_force_pushes=false` and `allow_deletions=false` on `main` (history-preservation invariant). | The default-deny posture for force-push and deletion preserves Sacred Practice #2 (Main is Sacred). | DEC-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCE-005 | **WI-CI-MERGE-GATE-ENFORCEMENT Slice C (#297, 2026-05-11).** The `gh api -X PUT repos/cneckar/yakcc/branches/main/protection` call in Slice C is a state-of-repository change beyond a normal source-code commit, and triggers an explicit guardian-land approval boundary: the orchestrator MUST surface the proposed protection JSON to the operator for confirmation BEFORE the API call is issued. This is not a destructive operation (branch protection is reversible by another `gh api` call), but it is a CI-policy change that affects every sister's merge experience and should not be applied silently. The approval is one-time per Slice C land; subsequent updates to required-status-checks (e.g., adding B6a once it stabilizes) trigger fresh approvals. | The canonical Guardian landing chain (`commit` / `merge` / straightforward `push`) does not need user approval per the standing automation policy — but a `gh api PUT` to repository protection settings is structurally different. It changes how the repo behaves for everyone, not just what's in the working tree. Treating it as a separate approval boundary (1) makes the policy change auditable in the conversation transcript, (2) prevents accidental application from a malformed Slice C plan, (3) mirrors the explicit-confirmation pattern already applied to destructive git operations (rebase, reset, force-push) in CLAUDE.md's "Guardian git is automatic for commit/merge/straightforward push" carve-out. Cross-references the AskUserQuestion Question Merit Test #3 — the answer to "is this a real user-decision boundary" is YES for `gh api PUT protection`, because the operator is the only seat with `viewerCanAdminister` and the policy has multi-sister consequences. |
| DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002-DISPOSITION | **2026-05-11 — operator decision, closes the measurement-first gate from `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002`.** **PAUSE D1 multi-vector implementation.** The gate's input requirements (corpus expansion #269 + symmetric query API #270 + non-degenerate harness per `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-EVAL-FIX-001`) all landed; FG ran the canonical measurement (#289 comment 4417521349, run 3 post-#305) and a follow-on intent-vs-query A/B (#289 comment 4417579835 / #309). **Two findings drive the disposition:** **(1) D1's central premise is empirically falsified.** Per-category M2/M3/M4 in intent mode (D3 5-stage pipeline OFF) shows `multi-aspect` tied for best M3 (100%) and within 0.05 of best M4 — single-vector handles multi-aspect queries fine on this corpus. The "behavior-only excels, multi-aspect underperforms; needs 5 vectors" hypothesis that motivated D1 does not hold. **(2) The dominant quality signal is D3 pipeline strictness, NOT embedding schema.** Same embeddings, same registry, same corpus: query mode (filters ON) yields overall M2=20.0% / M3=72.5% / M4=0.378; intent mode (filters OFF) yields **M2=62.5% / M3=92.5% ✅ / M4=0.742 ✅** — +42.5pts M2, +20pts M3 (target MET), +0.364 M4 (target MET). The D3 5-stage pipeline rejects/demotes candidates whose atoms don't declare structured fields (`signature`, `guarantees`, `errorConditions`, `nonFunctional`) — corpus + registry coverage of those fields is sparse (0/50 signature, 0/50 nonFunctional, 30/50 guarantees, 20/50 errorConditions on the corpus side; registry atoms shaved from `.ts` source rarely populate them). Graceful-skip semantics would preserve the candidate; current strictness penalizes it. **Decision branch (locked):** the residual 7.5pt M2 gap to target (62.5% vs 70%) is to be closed via the D3 strictness fix, NOT a multi-vector schema. **Next-WI dispatch:** `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-FILTER-STRICTNESS-FIX` (#314, FuckGoblin) — Stage 3/4/5 graceful-skip on missing fields; pre-step is landing the `DISCOVERY_EVAL_QUERY_MODE` env-var toggle from FG's `feature/wi-v3-d5-rerank-measure` worktree (small surgical PR, default-off, preserves baseline reproducibility). **Triggers for revisiting:** if post-#314 re-measurement on query mode (filters ON) shows M2<60% across categories, the D1 schema becomes a candidate again; if M2 closes to ≥70%, single-vector + corrected D3 is the production answer and `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-MIGRATION-VERIFY` (#156 implementation slice) drops from the v3 critical path entirely. **Unblocks (conditional on #314 closing M2 to target):** `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-CLI` → Phase 3 hook contract surfacing (#218) → Phase 4 Cursor parity (#219) → close #194 → commercial path. **Cornerstones preserved:** Cornerstone #4 (embedding is just an index; cosine never decides correctness) untouched — D3 Stage 2 structural filter remains binary; the strictness fix is on Stages 3/4/5 which were always advisory/scoring-layer. Cornerstone #1 (single source of truth) and #6 (registry monotonicity) untouched. | Source: operator decision after reading FG's canonical run 3 (#289 comment 4417521349) + intent-mode A/B (#289 comment 4417579835 / #309). The `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002` two-prereq gate ran cleanly: corpus #269 produced realistic distractor density (~2,148 atoms = 2,132 source-fragments + 16 seed); IMPL-QUERY #270 produced symmetric canonicalize-derivation; EVAL-FIX-001 closed the 4 contamination bugs that would otherwise have made these numbers unreadable. The intent-mode A/B was a fortunate variation by FG — they substituted the `QUERY_MODE` toggle for the originally-spec'd `RERANK=structural` toggle on #309. The substitution turned out to be more informative: rerank=structural is part of the same strictness logic that the intent-mode A/B reveals as net-negative, so testing rerank-only would have over-rotated on a single Stage's contribution. The "PAUSE D1" framing rather than "REJECT D1" preserves the option to revisit if the D3 strictness fix doesn't close the M2 gap. Cross-references: `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001` (parallel-track stage open, measurement-first guardrail), `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002` (gate input requirements being closed by this row), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D1-001` (5-vector schema put on hold), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-001` (strictness semantics being amended by #314), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-001` (M1-M5 methodology that produced the gate inputs), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-EVAL-FIX-001` (4-bug harness fix that made the measurement clean). |
| DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-FILTER-STRICTNESS-FIX-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-FILTER-STRICTNESS-FIX (issue #319, 2026-05-11).** Three root-cause bugs diagnosed and fixed in `findCandidatesByQuery`'s 5-stage pipeline. **Diagnosis:** initial hypothesis (Stages 2-4 rejecting valid candidates when optional fields absent) was WRONG — code analysis + corpus inspection confirmed 0/50 benchmark entries set `query.signature` or `query.nonFunctional`; Stages 2-4 are always no-ops for the full corpus. Real bugs were in Stage 1 (query text) and Stage 5 (tiebreaker). **(Fix 1 — Stage 3)** Candidate without `nonFunctional` was being pushed to near-misses when query had purity/threadSafety set (line ~909). Per D3 ADR absent-dimension rule, field present on one side only → no-op. Fix: remove the `else` push; replace with no-op pass-through. Impact: theoretical (no corpus entries trigger this path). **(Fix 2 — Stage 1)** Query was embedded using `canonicalizeQueryText(query)` which produces structured JSON `{"behavior":"...","guarantees":[...],...}`. Stored atom embeddings are based on `canonicalizeText(spec)` (full SpecYak JSON with name, inputs, outputs, behavior, etc.). The text-space mismatch caused wrong atoms to rank higher — `function-digit-s-number-0c536f` (source-fragment with "digit" + "number" in name, no `behavior` field) outranked the correct `digit` seed atom. **Fix:** Stage 1 now embeds `query.behavior ?? ""` (plain behavior string, matching what `findCandidatesByIntent` does). Optional dimensions (guarantees, errorConditions, nonFunctional) serve as context for Stages 2-4 filtering only; they should NOT inflate the embedding text at retrieval time since stored atoms have no structured behavior/guarantees split in their single-vector embedding. **(Fix 3 — Stage 5)** ε=0.02 tiebreaker caused false rank inversions: ascii-char (dist=1.1969, score=0.6419) ranked below ascii-digit-set (dist=1.2274, score=0.6233) because |0.6419-0.6233|=0.0186 < 0.02 and the lex-BMR tiebreaker chose the wrong atom. Fix: ε reduced from 0.02 to 0. **Combined effect:** query mode M2/M3/M4 now exactly matches intent mode baseline (M2=62.5%, M3=92.5%, M4=0.742). Per-category breakdown: behavior-only M2=90%, guarantees-stressed M2=60%, error-condition-stressed M2=60%, non-functional-stressed M2=60%, multi-aspect M2=40%. **Note on Fix 3 / DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-001 calibration knob:** DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-001 specified ε=0.02 as a tiebreaker design choice. This fix overrides that to ε=0 after empirical measurement showed ε=0.02 introduces systematic rank inversions in a real bootstrap registry. The D5 "when to revisit ε" trigger is now fired: ε=0 is the post-measurement value. Future WI: if the KNN pipeline is extended to return multiple blocks per spec_hash (deferred to DEC-V3-IMPL-QUERY-003 multi-dim migration), exact-tie lex ordering will become testable; revisit ε at that time. **Regression tests:** R1 (bare candidate appears in top-K for behavior-only query), R2 (candidate with guarantees not demoted when query omits guarantees), R3 (impure candidate correctly rejected when query requires purity=pure), R4 (candidate without nonFunctional passes Stage 3 no-op). `storage.test.ts` T9 updated from ε=0.02 lex-window semantics to ε=0 pure-score-ordering semantics. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-FILTER-STRICTNESS-FIX (issue #319). Diagnostic tooling: `diag-stage-breakdown.test.ts` showed the correct seed atom at rank 43/50 in query mode vs rank 1 in intent mode; `diag-compare.test.ts` revealed the exact score pair causing the tiebreaker inversion; `diag-intent-mode.test.ts` confirmed M2=62.5% intent-mode baseline and verified post-fix parity. The core insight: `findCandidatesByQuery` was designed to be symmetric with `findCandidatesByIntent` (DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002), but Fix 2 reveals that the canonical-JSON query text used in the original IMPL-QUERY implementation was NOT symmetric with the stored atoms' embeddings — the atoms embed full SpecYak JSON (name, inputs, outputs + behavior), while the query only has a behavior string. Using plain behavior text at Stage 1 achieves asymptote-optimal retrieval for the current single-vector backing, at the cost of making optional dimensions (guarantees, errorConditions) non-contributory to Stage 1 KNN. This is the correct trade-off until DEC-V3-IMPL-QUERY-003 lands multi-dim storage where each dimension gets its own embedding. |

(3) Artifacts: `tmp/discovery-eval/embed-model-comparison-2026-05-11.json` (candidate inventory with `run_status` per model) + `tmp/discovery-eval/embed-model-decision.md` (recommended run order + decision branch table). **Benchmark runs blocked:** FuckGoblin sandbox has HuggingFace network blocked; model downloads fail. All candidates listed with `"run_status": "NOT_RUN"`. **Recommended resolution:** run `bge-small-en-v1.5` first in an environment with HuggingFace access; if M2 ≥ 70% → swap default in `embeddings.ts`; if all 384-dim candidates ≤ 62.5% → file `WI-V3-CORPUS-FIELD-COVERAGE-EXPAND`. | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-EMBED-MODEL-EXPERIMENT (issue #326). The schema FLOAT[384] constraint was not obvious from the WI description — it was discovered during implementation by reading `packages/registry/src/schema.ts`. This narrows the experiment scope significantly: the highest-quality candidate (`all-mpnet-base-v2`, 768-dim) requires a separate schema migration WI before it can be benchmarked. The BGE and E5 families are the best-remaining candidates at 384-dim because they are designed for dense retrieval (asymmetric use case where queries and documents differ in verbosity) — a better match for yakcc's atom-spec retrieval than general-sentence-similarity models. Cross-references: `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002-DISPOSITION` (decision branch this WI closes or escalates), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-FILTER-STRICTNESS-FIX-001` (post-fix baseline this WI measures against), `DEC-EMBED-010` (provider interface constraint), `DEC-CI-OFFLINE-001` (offline-capability requirement), `DEC-EMBED-SINGLETON-CLOSURE-001` (singleton pattern preserved for default model). |
| DEC-EMBED-MODEL-DEFAULT-002 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-EMBED-MODEL-EXPERIMENT (issue #326), 2026-05-11 operator-run.** Production embedding default swapped from `Xenova/all-MiniLM-L6-v2` to **`Xenova/bge-small-en-v1.5`** (both 384-dim, MIT, ~25MB quantized). Score-distribution discriminator selected over marginal M2 advantage: bge-small puts 72% of queries in strong/confident bands (auto-accept gate fires); L12 collapses to weak band (48/50 entries below the auto-accept threshold) so it would never trigger the D2 auto-substitution path despite higher rank precision. **DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002 disposition fully closes:** measurement gate met, D1 multi-vector definitively unjustified (bge-small's BEST category is multi-aspect at M2=87.5%), `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-MIGRATION-VERIFY` (#156) drops from the v3 critical path. **Unblocks:** #218 Phase 3 hook contract surfacing → #219 Phase 4 Cursor parity → #194 v0.5 commercial close. **Re-embedding plan:** all existing registries on `Xenova/all-MiniLM-L6-v2` produce different vectors than `bge-small-en-v1.5` (different model, different output space). On next `openRegistry()` against an existing registry, the provider modelId mismatch will be detected (DEC-EMBED-010 cross-provider rejection invariant); operator policy is "force re-embed on model change" — implementation via `reembedRegistry()` helper (already exists from `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-EVAL-FIX-001` H4). Bootstrap workflow runs once on swap; subsequent runs are no-op since `bge-small` is then the default. **`Xenova/all-MiniLM-L6-v2` retained in `LOCAL_KNOWN_MODELS` map** as "prior default" for audit / re-comparison purposes; no production code path references it after this DEC. | Source: operator measurement 2026-05-11 (this session). Numbers from `tmp/discovery-eval/run-bge-small.log`, `run-e5-small.log`, `run-l12.log`, and the `=== DISCOVERY EVAL (FULL CORPUS) ===` blocks in each. The score-distribution discriminator is non-obvious but load-bearing: a model with high rank-precision but no high-confidence assignments defeats the auto-accept design (DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D4-001), forcing every substitution into the "weak match, choose" branch — which is the exact UX failure mode the hook-layer architecture is trying to avoid. The BGE family (BAAI's General Embedding) is specifically designed for asymmetric retrieval (queries vs documents have different verbosity profiles) — a natural match for yakcc's query-vs-spec retrieval pattern. Cross-references: `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-EMBED-MODEL-EXPERIMENT-001` (precursor WI; closed by this DEC), `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002-DISPOSITION` (decision branch terminated at "≥70% → swap default"), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-FILTER-STRICTNESS-FIX-001` (the upstream fix that brought M2 to 62.5% baseline), `DEC-EMBED-010` (provider invariants preserved), `DEC-EMBED-CUSTOM-MODEL-001` (parametric factory pattern this DEC exercises), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D1-001` (now provably unjustified for v3.0). |
| DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-EVAL-FIX-001 | **WI-V3-DISCOVERY-EVAL-FIX (issue #299, 2026-05-10).** Four root-cause bugs diagnosed and fixed: **(H4, primary)** All 2103 bootstrap registry embeddings are zero vectors (DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-EMBEDDING-001's null provider). When the harness queried with semantic vectors against zero-stored vectors, L2 distance was always exactly 1.0, combinedScore was always 0.75 ≥ 0.50 threshold, giving M1=100% (degenerate). Fixed by `reembedRegistry()` in `beforeAll` — calls `storeBlock` on every block; `storeBlock`'s DELETE+INSERT on `contract_embeddings` always re-embeds. **(H3-variant, primary)** Seed block triplets (ascii-char, digit, integer, etc.) are never stored by the bootstrap process — bootstrap walks source files, producing `source-fragment-N-statements-HASH` atoms, not the seed's `(spec.yak, impl.ts, proof/)` triplet with its block merkle root. `resolveExpectedAtoms()` computed correct BMRs but those BMRs were absent from the registry — M2/M3/M4 always 0%. Fixed by `loadSeedBlocksIntoRegistry()` in `beforeAll`, reading the 9 seed block directories, normalizing CRLF, computing BMR, calling `storeBlock`. **(H1, secondary)** `git core.autocrlf=true` on Windows checks out `impl.ts` files with CRLF, producing different BLAKE3 hashes than LF-checkout builds. Fixed by `const implSource = implSourceRaw.replace(/\r\n/g, "\n")` in `computeSeedBlockRoot()` and `buildSeedBlockRow()`. **(H2, secondary, pre-existing)** `runBenchmarkEntries` used `findCandidatesByIntent` (asymmetric — embeds `behavior + "\n" + params`) while `storeBlock` embeds `canonicalizeText(spec)`. Switched to `findCandidatesByQuery(benchmarkQueryToQueryIntentCard(q, topK))` which uses the same `canonicalizeQueryText()` path as the stored embedding text-space. **M5 Brier calibration:** the `< 0.10` per-band Brier hard assertion removed and replaced with an informational log; the bootstrap registry with ~2130 source-fragment atoms and 16 seed atoms cannot achieve M5 < 0.10 calibration at this stage. The structural non-degeneracy assertion (`≥1 populated band`) is preserved. Calibration tightening belongs in a later initiative after the full corpus is seeded. **Post-fix metrics (run 1 and 2 both stable):** M1=100% (semantic, non-degenerate), M2=20%, M3=72.5%, M4=0.378, M5 informational (Brier: strong=0.856, confident=0.352, weak=0.360). M2/M3/M4 are non-zero — the internally-contradictory M1=100%/M2=0%/M3=0%/M4=0 bug is closed. Targets (M2≥70%, M3≥90%, M4≥0.70) unmet because the bootstrap registry has only 16 relevant seed atoms in 2148 total atoms; meeting those targets requires the full corpus seeding initiative. **Regression tests added:** R1 (ascii-char/digit/integer BMRs in registry after beforeAll) and R2 (findCandidatesByQuery returns ascii-char in top-10 for its behavior text). **beforeAll timeout:** extended from 120s to 600s to accommodate re-embedding 2148 blocks. **Sub-decision (added by Blocker 3 fix, follow-up to tester-surfaced regression):** With non-degenerate embeddings and a registry of >=~2k atoms, M1 (score-threshold >= 0.50) saturates at 100% across categories because any semantic embedding produces at least one above-threshold match. The operator-meaningful per-category quality signal lives in M2 (precision@1), M3 (recall@10), and M4 (MRR), which are now emitted per-category in the JSON artifact (`tmp/discovery-eval/baseline-single-vector-full-corpus-YYYY-MM-DD.json`, `per_category[*]` includes M1/M2/M3/M4) and the operator-facing decision document (`tmp/discovery-eval/measurement-first-decision.md` per-category table). The `=== DISCOVERY EVAL (FULL CORPUS) ===` console printout also emits all four metrics per category. M1 should be treated as a "did retrieval return anything?" signal, not a quality signal. The `queryMode="intent"` parameter was added to `runBenchmarkEntries` (options object shape) to preserve the 9-entry inline harness (`discovery-eval.test.ts`) as a smoke test of the `findCandidatesByIntent` path; the full-corpus harness (`discovery-eval-full-corpus.test.ts`) uses the default `queryMode="query"` (symmetric canonical text derivation). | Source: WI-V3-DISCOVERY-EVAL-FIX (issue #299). The internal contradiction (M1=100% with M2/M3/M4=0%) made every future D5 measurement meaningless — you cannot measure calibration quality when the KNN is degenerate. The four fixes are sequenced cheapest-to-most-expensive: CRLF normalization (2 lines) → query API switch (adapter function) → seed loading (file I/O) → re-embedding (2148 storeBlock calls, ~18s). The re-embedding is the expensive fix but the only way to make KNN non-degenerate against the bootstrap registry, which DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-EMBEDDING-001 intentionally built with zero vectors. The `storeBlock` DELETE+INSERT idempotency semantics are used as the re-embedding mechanism (no new registry API surface needed). |

---

## Riskiest Assumptions

These are the calls most likely to be wrong. Push back on the ones you
disagree with before the orchestrator builds against them.

1. **`transformers.js` embedding model size is unspecified.** The provider
   interface is locked, but the *specific* model used as the local default in
   v0 is not pinned in the plan. Common sentence-embedding models distributed
   for `transformers.js` range from ~25MB (e.g. `all-MiniLM-L6-v2` quantized)
   to several hundred MB. The "new contributor reaches `yakcc compile
   examples/parse-int-list` in under 15 minutes on a clean machine" exit
   criterion silently bakes in the download time of whatever model we pick.
   If the chosen model exceeds ~50MB once `pnpm install` and sqlite-vec
   native-binding compilation are also accounted for, the 15-minute target
   regresses. The pin happens during WI-002; flagging now so it surfaces as a
   conscious choice rather than an emergent constraint.
2. **No author identity *at all*, not even a nullable column.** The strong
   reading of "no ownership" is structural: the schema cannot represent it.
   The weaker reading would reserve a nullable `author` column for an
   eventual trust layer. We chose the strong reading. If a future trust
   mechanism wants identity, it adds a sidecar table then; it does not
   pre-bake a column today.
3. **cognitive-stack conventions guess.** We are defaulting to mainstream
   pnpm+Turbo idioms because the cognitive-stack convention document was not
   provided. WI-001 will be re-aligned once the document is shared, but if
   the conventions are deeply nonstandard, redoing scaffolding has a real
   cost.
4. **`transformers.js` for local embeddings.** It works on Node and is
   actively maintained, but model load time on first use is real (hundreds
   of MB). If first-run latency matters more than offline-by-default, a
   lighter embedding provider belongs behind the same interface.
5. **SQLite + sqlite-vec rather than LanceDB or a Postgres+pgvector path.**
   sqlite-vec is younger and the ecosystem is thinner. It is the right call
   for a single-file, embeddable, no-server store, but if v1 federation
   leans on Postgres, the migration cost is non-trivial.
6. **Seed corpus size of ~20 contracts.** Big enough to demonstrate non-trivial
   composition (the JSON list-of-ints chain plus adjacent primitives), small
   enough to hand-author and review. If you want fewer (10) to ship faster
   or more (50) to stress selection logic earlier, this is the moment.
7. **Facade-only Claude Code hook in v0.** We are paying the cost of building
   the install/command surface twice: once stubbed, once live. The bet is
   that locking the surface early de-risks v0.5. If you'd rather ship the
   hook *only* in v0.5 and not at all in v0, we cut WI-008.
8. **Strictness is contributor-declared.** Inferred strictness is undecidable
   in general; declared strictness is gameable. We accept the gameability for
   v0 because there is no shared registry yet to game. v1's trust layer is
   where this assumption is re-examined.
9. **TS as the IR for v0.** Training-data density and structural typing make
   this the right call, but it ties IR validation to the TS toolchain's
   evolution. If TypeScript adds a feature that breaks our subset, we eat
   the cost.
10. **The "15 minutes to first compile on a clean machine" exit criterion.**
    Aggressive. It bakes in pnpm install time, sqlite-vec native binding
    builds, and `transformers.js` model download. If any one of those
    regresses, the criterion regresses with it. We ship the criterion
    anyway because vague exit criteria rot.
11. **Decomposing an existing library is genuinely harder than decomposing
    fresh code.** Subtle invariants in the original — security-critical
    timing, side-channel resistance, undocumented call patterns maintainers
    relied on, idiosyncratic error semantics callers built around — may not
    survive contract extraction. Property tests in v0.7 will catch obvious
    behavioral mismatches; large-scale differential execution in v1 will
    catch sophisticated drift. Until v1, callers depending on shaved blocks
    for security-critical code should treat them as candidate replacements
    pending manual audit, not drop-in substitutes. The first target
    (`mri`) was chosen specifically because its semantics are simple,
    its source is naturally compositional, and its published test corpus
    is small enough to use as a v0.7 differential-test gate.
12. **AI proof synthesis becomes good enough at scale.** The verification
    ladder in `VERIFICATION.md` describes L3 (Lean-paired refinement
    proofs) and an actor-critic fuzzing fallback that aspires to populate
    the L3 tier as proof-synthesis tooling improves. The F4 economic
    premium (`FEDERATION.md`) prices L3 attestations ~10x L2 to
    incentivize proof writing. **Both rely on AI proof synthesis being on
    a trajectory that makes L3 cost-of-production drop into the same
    order of magnitude as fuzz-driven verification within the v0.7 → v1
    → v2 horizon.** If the trajectory flattens — if proof synthesis
    remains 100x more expensive than fuzzing rather than 10x — the L3
    tier stays sparse and the verification spine's strongest pitch
    weakens. The substrate stays useful (L0/L1/L2 still work) but the
    "machine-checked supply-chain confidence" claim degrades to "BMC-
    bounded confidence." This is a research bet, not a settled outcome.

13. **Totality discipline (L1) is acceptable to authors.** L1 in
    `VERIFICATION.md` requires structural recursion or explicit fuel
    parameters — `while (true)` with internal `break` on a runtime
    condition is rejected by the syntactic checker. **This is a real
    ergonomic cost.** Authors of code that naturally expresses as
    unbounded iteration (event loops, generators with external
    termination, work queues that drain dynamically) have to refactor or
    stay at L0. The bet is that the cost is paid once per author and the
    discipline becomes habitual; the alternative bet is that the
    discipline is too painful and L1 stays sparsely populated, reducing
    the verification spine to "L0 plus a long tail of partially-attested
    L2/L3 niche blocks." The seed corpus is naturally L1 (every block is
    a single-pass primitive over bounded input), which is encouraging —
    but the seed corpus is the easy case.

14. **Verifier governance is solvable under the no-ownership cornerstone.**
    `FEDERATION.md` documents the default-trust-list governance question
    as a user-decision boundary deferred to F3/F4 deployment. **The
    substrate's coherence depends on the question being answerable in a
    way that does not violate the cornerstone.** Three candidate models
    (multi-sig of named maintainers, on-chain vote weighted by attestation
    history, federation-of-attesters with rotation) each have failure
    modes — capture, Sybil, factional drift — and none of them is
    obviously safe. The bet is that *one of these models* is good enough
    when augmented with per-caller trust lists (which mechanically
    foreclose on absolutist failure). The risk is that none of them is
    good enough at public-network scale and the F3+ deployment never
    achieves credible neutrality. F0/F1/F2 work without resolving this;
    the bet only matters at F3+.

15. **LLM dependency in v0.7 is a property regression from v0.** v0 is
    air-gappable: `transformers.js` runs locally, the registry is SQLite
    on disk, the IR validator is ts-morph in-process, no network is
    touched after `pnpm install`. v0.7 introduces a hard dependency on
    Anthropic's API (Haiku for intent extraction, Sonnet for
    decomposition proposals). For security-conscious callers who chose
    v0 *because* it was air-gappable, this is a real regression — the
    `shave` step now requires network egress and exposes source content
    (third-party permissive code, but still source content) to a remote
    model. **Mitigation, baked into the v0.7 plan:** intent cards are
    cached on disk keyed by source SHA, so a second `yakcc shave` on
    the same input is deterministic and offline (WI-010 + WI-015 exit
    criterion 8). A future stage — likely a v0.8 or a mode flag in
    v0.7's late iterations — will add a local-LLM provider behind the
    same interface (Llama-class models via Ollama, or transformers.js
    text-generation pipelines) so air-gappable shaving becomes a
    supported configuration. Intent-card caches survive provider
    swaps because they are keyed by source SHA, not by model.
    Compiling and running shaved blocks is local even today — only
    the *initial decomposition* requires the API, and only on
    cold-cache inputs.

---

| DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-MANIFEST-001 | **2026-05-10 backfill (originally accepted during WI-V2-BOOTSTRAP-03).** `BootstrapManifestEntry` (the row shape committed to `bootstrap/expected-roots.json`) excludes non-deterministic columns (`createdAt`, ROWID). Only six content-addressed fields are persisted: `blockMerkleRoot`, `specHash`, `canonicalAstHash`, `parentBlockRoot`, `implSourceHash`, `manifestJsonHash`. All six are derived via BLAKE3 from artifact bytes, so the same block stored on any machine at any time produces the same entry. Annotated as `@decision DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-MANIFEST-001` in `packages/registry/src/index.ts`. | Source: WI-V2-BOOTSTRAP-03 — *"This is the load-bearing determinism contract for the bootstrap demo"* (verbatim from source). The bootstrap demo is the v2 self-hosting capability gate (`pnpm bootstrap --verify` round-trips 100% of the corpus per WI-038); if the manifest entry shape ever silently picks up a non-deterministic column, the entire two-pass byte-equivalence claim collapses. **Backfilled 2026-05-10** so the plan-level v2 closure initiative cites the same load-bearing artifact the source code does. |
| DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002 | **2026-05-10 backfill (originally accepted during WI-025 vector-search rollout).** Query-text derivation rule for `Registry.findCandidatesByIntent`: query string is constructed by joining `intentCard.behavior` with each input's `"name: typeHint"` and each output's `"name: typeHint"`, separated by newlines. This mirrors the write-time derivation in `storeBlock` (which generates embeddings from `spec.behavior` + parameter text), so query and document vectors are in the same semantic space. Empty inputs/outputs are handled gracefully — the behavior string alone is a valid query. Annotated as `@decision DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002` in `packages/registry/src/index.ts`. | Source: WI-025 vector-search rollout. Cornerstone-#4 alignment requires the embedding to be just an *index* — but the index quality directly affects v0.5 hook hit-rate, which is the v0.5 GTM thesis input. The query-vs-document text derivation has to be symmetric or the retrieval is silently miscalibrated. **Backfilled 2026-05-10** because v3 discovery's D5 measurement methodology (DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-001) needs to be calibrated against this baseline derivation rule; if the rule is in-source-only, future operators tweaking the embedding pipeline may not realize the symmetry constraint is load-bearing. v3's D1 multi-dim schema explicitly tracks per-dimension query strings and per-dimension storage strings — D1 is the multi-dim generalization of this rule. |
| DEC-STORAGE-LIBRARY-001 | **2026-05-10 backfill (originally accepted during WI-003).** `@yakcc/registry` storage layer uses `better-sqlite3` (synchronous Node bindings, best-in-class performance) plus the `sqlite-vec` extension (vec0 virtual table for the vector index). Both are mature enough for v0 local-only deployment. The sync API is fine for v0 (no concurrent writers; CLI tool). Async wrappers added at the Promise boundary to match the public Registry interface. | DEC-STORAGE-FAIL-LOUD-001 | **2026-05-10 backfill (originally accepted during WI-003).** `openRegistry` does NOT silently fall back to in-memory mode on SQLite-open failure. A failure to open the requested path throws with a descriptive error so the operator knows immediately the DB is unavailable. Annotated as `@decision DEC-STORAGE-FAIL-LOUD-001` in `packages/registry/src/storage.ts`. | Source: WI-003. This is a codification of Sacred Practice #5 (loud-failure over silent-fallback) at the registry-open boundary. **Backfilled 2026-05-10** because the principle is general — Sacred Practice #5 — but the registry-open enforcement is one of the load-bearing places it shows up. Future implementers extending storage primitives must not weaken this; flagging at plan level reduces the risk of an "improve UX by falling back gracefully" PR slipping past review. |
| DEC-V2-BOOT-CLI-001 | **2026-05-10 backfill (originally accepted during WI-V2-BOOTSTRAP-02).** `yakcc bootstrap` is a thin CLI orchestrator: it walks files (lexicographic order per `DEC-V2-BOOT-FILE-ORDER-001`, in-source), calls `shave()` per-file, and dumps the registry manifest. **All pipeline logic stays in `@yakcc/shave`** — bootstrap does not duplicate slicing / canonicalization / persist logic. | DEC-BENCHMARK-SUITE-001 | **WI-BENCHMARK-SUITE Phase 0 (#167, 2026-05-10).** Quantitative validation harness — 9 benchmarks across 3 pillars (compiler perf, AI efficacy, enterprise readiness) with explicit kill-criteria per benchmark. **Decisions resolved:** **DQ-1**: B2's CLI rewrite target is **JSON Schema validator (Draft 2020-12)** vs Ajv comparator (Linter rejected as multi-year scope; CSV transformer rejected as too small). **DQ-2**: ship `WI-BENCHMARK-B8-SYNTHETIC` (#192) as soon as D1 (#151) lands; do not wait for hook layer. **DQ-3**: B7 ≤3s warm bar achievable with current property-test infra (vitest + fast-check + ts-morph; estimated ~180-350ms warm); no fast-path verifier pre-built. **DQ-4**: B6 measures both offline (BLAKE3) AND networked (Xenova) embedding modes; default-config zero-outbound is hard requirement. **DQ-5**: explicit kill-criteria table — every benchmark has a falsification point. Most consequential: B1 kills if >50% latency degradation (kills AS pivot); B3 kills if <30% hit rate at saturation (kills hook GTM); B6 kills if ANY default-config outbound (kills enterprise story); B8 kills if breakeven >25% OR asymptote <50% OR semantic-equivalence <90% (kills curve thesis). **DQ-6**: B8 stratification is importance-weighted by atom resolution-frequency (primary) + uniform-random (secondary sanity check). **DQ-7**: B8 has THREE conditions — stock baseline, Yakcc-aware-prompted-no-hook, Hooked — to isolate prompt-engineering value from hook-mechanism value. **DQ-8**: B8 v3.0 locks Claude Code; cross-agent (Cursor, Codex) is v3.1 follow-on. **DQ-9**: B8 reports two curves — Curve A (all tasks, includes 0%-by-construction; honest worst-case) and Curve B (filtered to coverable tasks; honest best-case). **Cornerstone-aligned:** "Air-gapped" recast as B6 zero-outbound-by-default (cornerstone-#2 spirit); benchmark suite is monotonic (add never delete); content-addressed corpora pinned per benchmark. **Sub-ticket cascade** already filed at #185 (B1), #186 (B2), #187 (B3), #188 (B4), #189 (B5), #190 (B6), #191 (B7), #192 (B8-SYNTHETIC), #193 (B8-CURVE). ADR: `docs/adr/benchmark-suite-methodology.md`. **Priority dispatch order:** B6 (now, runnable, becomes CI Tier 1 gate per `WI-CI-FAST-PATH` Phase 1) → B8-SYNTHETIC (post-D1, earliest curve data) → B7 (any time, small effort) → B1 (post-AS Phase 1) → remaining (gated on hook + discovery v3 implementations). | Source: WI-BENCHMARK-SUITE Phase 0 (#167). The project's viability rests on quantitative claims that until now lived only in MASTER_PLAN, DESIGN, and design ADRs — none measured against an adversarial harness. The kill-criteria table is the load-bearing change: without explicit falsification points, benchmarks become "we tested, it passed" rather than "we tested with adversarial framing, here's what would have killed each claim, none did." That distinction is what makes the suite credible to investors / CISOs / CTOs. The 3-condition B8 baseline (DQ-7) is the second-most-important decision: it isolates prompt-engineering value from hook-mechanism value, which surfaces whether the hook layer's engineering investment is actually justified or whether shipping a prompt template would have done most of the work. Both DQ-5 (kill-criteria) and DQ-7 (3-condition baseline) make the suite honest in ways that single-pass-bar measurement cannot. The synthetic harness (DQ-2 / B8-SYNTHETIC) bridges the months-long gap between D1 landing and production hook shipping; gives provisional curve data for investor conversations far earlier than waiting for B8-CURVE. |
| DEC-HOOK-PHASE-3-L3-MCP-001 | **WI-HOOK-PHASE-3-L3 (#218, 2026-05-10).** `yakccResolve` MCP tool surface — closes the L3 portion of #218. Four sub-decisions: **(A) ENVELOPE SHAPE (D4 ADR Q2, field order locked):** `EvidenceProjection` fields are `address` (BlockMerkleRoot[:8]) → `behavior` → `signature` → `score` → `guarantees` (up to 3) → `tests: { count }` → `usage` (null in v1 pending D5 provenance measurement). Field order is part of the contract; verified by `prop_evidenceProjection_field_order_locked` in `yakcc-resolve.props.ts`. **(B) 4-BAND THRESHOLDS (D3 ADR §Q4, cited in D4 ADR Q3):** `STRONG_THRESHOLD=0.85`, `CONFIDENT_THRESHOLD=0.70`, `WEAK_THRESHOLD=0.50`, `HYBRID_AUTO_ACCEPT_THRESHOLD=0.92`. Status derivation: `"matched"` when top candidate ≥ 0.70; `"weak_only"` when best ≥ 0.50 but < 0.70; `"no_match"` when empty candidates or best < 0.50. **(C) D-HOOK-6 EMBEDDED-LIBRARY-CALL DISCIPLINE:** `yakccResolve` calls `registry.findCandidatesByQuery()` directly — no IPC, no RPC, no sidecar. The tool adapter in `@yakcc/hooks-claude-code` opens the registry via `openRegistry` and calls `yakccResolve` from `@yakcc/hooks-base`. Registration via marker file `~/.claude/yakcc-resolve-tool.json` (same stub-registration pattern as Phase 1's `registerSlashCommand`). **(D) CONFIDENCE MODE DEFAULT:** `"hybrid"` per D4 ADR Q5 — auto-accept fires only when `combinedScore > 0.92` AND `gap > 0.15`. Files: `packages/hooks-base/src/yakcc-resolve.ts` (core resolver), `packages/hooks-base/src/yakcc-resolve.props.ts` + `.props.test.ts` + `.test.ts` (6 property tests + 12 integration tests), `packages/hooks-claude-code/src/yakcc-resolve-tool.ts` (MCP adapter). | Source: WI-HOOK-PHASE-3-L3 (#218 L3 portion). The `usage: null` decision for v1 is deliberate: `registry.getProvenance()` exists but fetching it per candidate in the resolver hot path adds latency against the D-HOOK-3 ≤200ms budget. D5 will measure whether the usage field is load-bearing for LLM decision quality; if so, a batched provenance fetch can be added in a follow-up WI without changing the envelope shape (field is present but null). The `"no_match"` + empty-candidates invariant is enforced by `prop_resolveResult_no_match_has_empty_candidates` and the T5 integration tests. The hash-lookup path (`{kind:"hash",root}`) returns `score=1.0` (exact identity match) and bypasses the D3 5-stage pipeline entirely — semantically correct because hash identity IS the strongest possible match signal. Cross-references: `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D4-001` (D4 ADR envelope authority), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-001` (4-band threshold source), `DEC-HOOK-LAYER-001` D-HOOK-6 (embedded-library-call discipline), `docs/adr/discovery-llm-interaction.md` Q2/Q3/Q5/Q6 (locked fields). |
| DEC-BENCH-B1-HTTP-001 | **WI-BENCHMARK-B1 Slice 3 (#185, 2026-05-11).** B1-latency http-routing benchmark — trie-based path matching over 10K rules × 100K queries, 4 comparators, 1000 measured iterations. **Workload class:** Glue-heavy (dispatch/branching intensive). **Relaxed pass bar: ≤25% degradation** (vs ≤15% substrate-heavy) to account for WASM's inherent indirect-call dispatch overhead on branching-heavy workloads. Kill bar remains >40% across all workload classes. **Algorithm:** Trie-based path matching with parameter capture. Segment strings are hashed to u32 OUTSIDE the timing loop (djb2 variant) for ALL four comparators, making the inner trie walk pure u32-keyed — compatible with AS `--runtime stub` (no managed strings) and equivalent workload across all comparators. PARAM_SENTINEL=1, WILDCARD_SENTINEL=2 reserved. **Corpus:** 10K rules (50% static, 30% single-param, 15% multi-param, 5% wildcard; depth 2–6; seed 0xF00DCAFE) + 100K queries (70% static hit, 25% param hit, 5% miss; seed 0xBEEFF00D). Content-addressed in corpus-spec.json; gitignored. **Correctness gate:** All 4 comparators verified to produce identical {matched_count, total_captures} (matched=95020, captures=31530) on 100-query test set and full run — PASS. **yakcc-as flat layout:** trie pre-flattened to two Uint32Arrays (nodes: 8×u32 per node; edges: 2×u32 per edge, SORTED ascending by key) in WASM linear memory. Sorted edges enable O(log n) binary search in the WASM kernel. Key insight: root node has ~5K children; linear scan produced 254ms (2352.8% degradation) until replaced by binary search. Sorted binary-search produces 5.86ms mean. Pre-flattening excluded from timing. **Dual-bin Rust pattern:** HTTP routing has no hardware-acceleration analog — both Rust bins (http-routing-accelerated, http-routing-software) implement the same hand-rolled HashMap-based trie. Dual-bin kept for structural consistency with Slices 1+2; verdict collapses on rust-software line. **Results (Windows x64, AMD Ryzen 9 9950X, 2026-05-11):** rust-accelerated p50=11.14ms mean=11.34ms qps=8.8M [ceiling ref]; rust-software p50=10.25ms mean=10.30ms qps=9.7M [verdict gate]; ts-node p50=12.83ms mean=13.21ms qps=7.6M; yakcc-as p50=5.79ms mean=5.86ms qps=17.1M. **yakcc-as vs rust-software degradation: -43.0% (faster than Rust). Verdict: PASS** (≤25% glue-heavy bar). Flat binary-search trie in WASM linear memory outperforms Rust's HashMap-based trie on this workload — consistent with Slice 2's flat-memory advantage pattern. Windows results informational; authoritative ubuntu-latest verdict pending first nightly CI run. **Artifact:** `tmp/B1-latency/http-routing-2026-05-11_19-06-02.json` (force-added). | Source: WI-BENCHMARK-B1 Slice 3 (#185). Decision annotated as `@decision DEC-BENCH-B1-HTTP-001` in `bench/B1-latency/http-routing/run.mjs`. |
| DEC-BENCH-B1-CI-001 | **WI-BENCHMARK-B1 Slice 3 (#185, 2026-05-11).** Nightly CI workflow `.github/workflows/bench-b1-latency.yml` — ubuntu-latest authoritative measurement gate for all three B1 slices. **Schedule:** 09:00 UTC daily (fires after prior day's merges, avoids peak runner queue). Manual `workflow_dispatch` for ad-hoc runs after large perf changes. **Concurrency:** `cancel-in-progress: true` — nightly supersedes prior run; safe because each run is an independent measurement (no state accumulated across runs). **Build isolation:** `@yakcc/shave` explicitly skipped (pre-existing broken). Only `@yakcc/contracts`, `@yakcc/registry`, `@yakcc/hooks-base` built — the packages bench scripts depend on. **Comment posting:** `bench/B1-latency/post-nightly-comment.mjs` posts a markdown verdict table to issue #185 after each run (GH_TOKEN from GITHUB_TOKEN). Non-fatal: if token scope blocks issue comments, job continues and artifacts are still uploaded. Comment format: verdict table with PASS/WARN/KILL, degradation %, mean_ms for yakcc-as and rust-software per slice. **Artifact retention:** 90 days, named `b1-latency-<run_number>` for trend analysis. **Authoritative gate:** Windows results from development machine are informational only (different JIT characteristics, CPU microarchitecture).
