| DEC-BENCH-B1-INTEGER-001 | **WI-BENCHMARK-B1 Slice 1 (#185, 2026-05-11) — corrected verdict 2026-05-11.** B1-latency integer-math benchmark — SHA-256 over 100MB corpus, 4 comparators, 1000 measured iterations. **3-slice strategy:** B1 split into Slice 1 (integer-math / SHA-256, this WI), Slice 2 (JSON, deferred), Slice 3 (HTTP + CI, deferred) for incremental delivery. **Methodology:** xorshift32 corpus (seed 0xDEADBEEF, 100MB, SHA-256 content-addressed); 100 warm-up + 1000 measured iterations per comparator; each comparator runs as a fresh subprocess; environment tag (platform/arch/cpu/node/rust/yakcc_head) on every artifact. **Dual-comparator discipline:** Cargo features apply at the whole-crate build level; two separate cargo invocations produce `rust-baseline-accelerated` (cpufeatures SHA-NI runtime dispatch, ceiling reference) and `rust-baseline-software` (sha2 `force-soft` feature, pure-Rust path, apples-to-apples gate). The verdict gate is yakcc-as vs rust-software, NOT yakcc-as vs rust-accelerated — both run the same pure-software RFC 6234 SHA-256 algorithm. **Results (Windows x64, AMD Ryzen 9 9950X, 2026-05-11):** rust-accelerated (sha2 cpufeatures, SHA-NI) p50=37.94ms mean=38.00ms tp=2632MB/s [ceiling reference]; rust-software (sha2 force-soft, pure-Rust) p50=171.30ms mean=173.43ms tp=577MB/s [verdict gate]; ts-node (Node crypto/OpenSSL) p50=38.09ms mean=38.15ms tp=2621MB/s; yakcc-as (WASM pure-software SHA-256) p50=258.83ms mean=267.96ms tp=373MB/s. **Speedup rust-accelerated vs rust-software: +356%** (confirms SHA-NI disabled in software binary). **yakcc-as vs rust-software degradation: +54.5%** (pass bar ≤15%, kill bar >40%). **Verdict: KILL** — yakcc-as WASM is 54.5% slower than pure-software Rust running the same algorithm, exceeding the >40% kill bar. Artifact: `tmp/B1-latency/integer-math-2026-05-11_17-26-42.json` (committed with `git add --force`). **Interpretation:** The KILL verdict is the correct apples-to-apples result. rust-software uses the same pure-Rust SHA-256 implementation path as yakcc-as WASM — neither uses SHA-NI. The 54.5% gap is the WASM JIT overhead for this workload on this platform (Windows/x64, Node v22, Ryzen 9 9950X). The earlier 3-comparator run (+617% vs SHA-NI-accelerated Rust) was a methodologically incorrect comparison that conflated JIT overhead with hardware acceleration gap. The corrected KILL verdict triggers re-plan of #143 AS initiative per the defined kill criterion. Windows results are informational; the authoritative gate runs on GitHub Actions ubuntu-latest (x86-64). | Source: WI-BENCHMARK-B1 Slice 1 (#185). Decision annotated as `@decision DEC-BENCH-B1-INTEGER-001` in `bench/B1-latency/integer-math/run.mjs`. |
| DEC-HOOK-LAYER-001 | **WI-HOOK-LAYER Phase 0 (#194, 2026-05-10).** Six load-bearing decisions for the v0.5+ AI-agent hook layer. **D-HOOK-1**: first IDE target is **Claude Code** (Cursor Phase 4; Codex Phase 5 conditional; agnostic/proxy mode rejected without demand signal). **D-HOOK-2**: interception at the **tool-call layer** (Edit/Write/MultiEdit) — not file-write or prompt-rewrite. **D-HOOK-3**: **synchronous** atom resolution with hard ≤200ms p95 latency budget; budget violations are discovery-side regressions, not async escape hatches. **D-HOOK-4**: contract surfacing via **inline contract comment** (`// @atom <name> (<sig>; <key-guarantee>) — yakcc:<hash[:8]>`) preserving multi-turn LLM coherence; opaque-hash and sidecar-file alternatives rejected on B5 grounds. **D-HOOK-5**: telemetry **local-only by default** (`~/.yakcc/telemetry/<session-id>.jsonl`); intent text is BLAKE3-hashed before storage; no PII; opt-in upload via `YAKCC_TELEMETRY_UPLOAD_URL` only. Cornerstone-bound (no-ownership preserved). B6 air-gapped CI gate (#190) enforces zero-outbound-by-default. **D-HOOK-6**: discovery integration is an **embedded library call** (workspace dep on `@yakcc/registry`) — not IPC, not RPC, not sidecar daemon. Bridge from existing v0/v1 hook (`DEC-HOOK-BASE-001`'s `executeRegistryQuery`) is **additive across phases**, not a rewrite. ADR: `docs/adr/hook-layer-architecture.md`. Implementation cascade filed as Phase 1–5 sub-tickets of #194. | Source: WI-HOOK-LAYER Phase 0 (#194). The hook layer is the user-facing surface — without it, yakcc is a registry plus a CLI. Five of nine project benchmarks (B3 #187, B4 #188, B5 #189, B7 #191, B8-CURVE #193) gate on hook existence; the v0.5 GTM thesis cannot be measured without it. The Phase 0 ADR locks the architecture before implementation starts so all five Phase-N implementations cite the same load-bearing decisions and produce a single-mechanism (no parallel surfaces, no protocol drift between phases). All six decisions preserve the cornerstones: D-HOOK-3 keeps cosine out of selection (preserves cornerstone #4 — embedding is just an index); D-HOOK-5 keeps telemetry local-by-default (preserves cornerstone #2 — no ownership); D-HOOK-6 composes via minimal blocks (preserves cornerstone #5). The migration from current v0 facade is staged: Phase 1 retires the marker-file pattern + adds telemetry; Phase 2 adds substitution; Phase 3 adds contract surfacing; Phase 4/5 add IDE adapters. Each phase ships independent measurable value. |
| DEC-AS-MULTI-EXPORT-001 | **WI-AS-PHASE-2-COVERAGE Phase 2A.0 (#146, PR #224, 2026-05-10).** `assemblyScriptBackend()` emits one WASM export per shaved helper function in a multi-atom module, not a single fused entry. Implementation accepts `ResolutionResult.blocks` (Phase 1 accepted only the primary atom) and emits a top-level AS export for each helper that the wave-3 visitor would have rejected at its `missing-export` front gate. The 86 wave-3 "missing-export" pending atoms (98.9% of the wave-3 pending corpus) are AS-backend-eligible because AS handles multi-function modules natively without the wave-3 export-shape restriction. Annotated as `@decision DEC-AS-MULTI-EXPORT-001` in `packages/compile/src/as-backend.ts`. | Source: WI-AS-PHASE-2-COVERAGE Phase 2A.0 (#146). The dominant blocker for AS-backend coverage of the seed-block corpus was a measurement-methodology issue, not feature-complexity — wave-3's `closer-parity.test.ts` keys "covered" off wave-3 visitor success, which artificially restricts the AS-backend's measurable surface. Multi-export wiring + the sibling closer-parity test (`DEC-AS-CLOSER-PARITY-SIBLING-FILE-001`) together unblock the AS-backend's actual coverage trajectory. Phase 2A.0 is the first non-docs Wrath WI in the v3 design / Phase 1-2 sweep — Phase 1 (#145, PR #169) shipped the numeric-substrate MVP; Phase 2A.0 makes the multi-export emit production-ready and adds the measurement vehicle for sub-slices 2A.1–2I. |
| DEC-AS-CLOSER-PARITY-SIBLING-FILE-001 | **WI-AS-PHASE-2-COVERAGE Phase 2A.0 (#146, PR #224, 2026-05-10).** AS-backend parity tests live as sibling files alongside wave-3's tests, not merged into the existing wave-3 file. New test: `packages/compile/test/as-backend/closer-parity-as.test.ts` (mirrors structure of `examples/v1-wave-3-wasm-lower-demo/test/closer-parity.test.ts` but invokes `assemblyScriptBackend()` directly instead of going through wave-3 visitor). New registry: `examples/v1-wave-3-wasm-lower-demo/test/pending-atoms-as.json` (sibling of wave-3's `pending-atoms.json`; tracks AS-backend-specific failures with AS-relevant categories: `asc-compile-error`, `parity-mismatch`, `asc-timeout`, etc.). 80%-coverage gate stays `it.fails()` and rides on the sibling file until cumulative sub-slices 2A.1–2I cross the threshold. Wave-3 oracle (`closer-parity.test.ts`, `pending-atoms.json`) is read-only across all Phase 2 sub-slices; Phase 3 owns retirement. Annotated as `@decision DEC-AS-CLOSER-PARITY-SIBLING-FILE-001` in `packages/compile/test/as-backend/closer-parity-as.test.ts`. | Source: WI-AS-PHASE-2-COVERAGE Phase 2A.0 (#146). Modifying wave-3's closer-parity test to also exercise AS-backend would create a single test with two failure modes that report identically — operator can't tell which backend regressed. Sibling files preserve the differential-oracle role (wave-3 vs AS-backend can both fail/pass independently, and the test output identifies which). Sibling pending-atoms registries solve the same problem at the per-atom-failure level: AS-relevant failure categories don't pollute wave-3's category schema, and Phase 3 retirement of wave-3 doesn't churn the AS registry. |
| DEC-AS-RECORD-LAYOUT-001 | **WI-AS-PHASE-2-COVERAGE Phase 2A.0 (#146, PR #224, 2026-05-10).** AS-backend record substrate uses 8-byte stride for primitive fields, matching wave-3's record layout for differential-oracle parity. Implementation: AS classes mapped from TS object literal types via `@unmanaged` annotation; field offsets at 8-byte boundaries (i32 fields padded to 8 bytes, f64 fields naturally 8-byte aligned, nested-record fields use pointer indirection). Initial test corpus: R1 `sumRecord3` (3 i32 fields), R2 `mixedRecord` (i32+f64+i32), R3 `nestedRecord` (2-level pointer indirection). Each substrate verified via 20 fast-check runs against TS reference. Annotated as `@decision DEC-AS-RECORD-LAYOUT-001` in `packages/compile/test/as-backend/records-parity.test.ts`. | Source: WI-AS-PHASE-2-COVERAGE Phase 2A.0 (#146). Records arrived early as a bonus from the implementer overrun (operator-bounded slice was multi-export only; records were planner-deferred to follow-up `WI-AS-PHASE-2A1-RECORDS`). The 8-byte stride matches wave-3's existing record layout, which preserves the differential-oracle property: an atom that compiles to byte-equivalent (or value-equivalent for f64) WASM under both backends remains "covered" without backend-specific layout drift. R4–R6 (deeply nested, large struct, zero-sized/edge cases) and adversarial fast-check expansions are deferred to follow-up sub-slices.

| DEC-CI-FAST-PATH-PHASE-1-002 | **WI-CI-FAST-PATH Phase 1 (#196, 2026-05-10).** Affected-package detection uses `pnpm --filter "...[origin/<base-ref>]"` via a thin wrapper `scripts/affected-packages.sh`. Any hand-rolled file-to-package map would diverge from pnpm's truth. The wrapper exists only to (a) resolve the right base ref under GitHub Actions PR context (`$GITHUB_BASE_REF` or `origin/main` fallback) and (b) document the empty-affected case (docs-only PR returns 0 packages — no-op, exits 0). pnpm's `--filter "[ref]"` returns ALL workspace packages when `pnpm-lock.yaml` changes, making the Phase 2 "lockfile escape hatch" unnecessary in Phase 1. |
| DEC-CI-FAST-PATH-PHASE-1-003 | **WI-CI-FAST-PATH Phase 1 (#196, 2026-05-10).** lint and typecheck always run over the full workspace in pr-ci.yml. No affected-only optimization. | Biome lint + tsc are pure static analysis. On a 13-package monorepo with `cache: pnpm` warm, lint+typecheck total wall-clock is well under 60s. Running them only on affected packages risks missing a downstream type error in a consumer not in the diff (e.g., a public type rename in `@yakcc/contracts` breaks `@yakcc/registry` typecheck). Turbo's local cache skips unchanged packages automatically; in CI, the cost is minimal. |

The dominant runtime-reduction lever in Phase 1 is affected-package selection (typically 1–3 packages out of 13 on a representative PR). | DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX-002 | **2026-05-10 — supersedes the formula-related portions of `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX-001`.** PR #268's diagnosis (verified by orchestrator at `packages/registry/src/schema.ts:98,218` — vec0 declared with no `distance=` specifier defaults to L2 Euclidean) is the actual root cause of the M1=0% bug surfaced in PR #254. The previous `cosineDistanceToCombinedScore` formula `1 - d/2` was the correct mapping for cosine distance — but `d` is L2 distance, not cosine. For unit-normalized vectors, the identity `cosine_distance = (L2)² / 2` makes the correct combinedScore mapping `1 - L2²/4 = (1 + cos(θ)) / 2`. **Fix:** change `cosineDistanceToCombinedScore` to `Math.max(0, Math.min(1, 1 - (cosineDistance * cosineDistance) / 4))` AND restore `M1_HIT_THRESHOLD` from 0.40 back to 0.50 (D3 Q5's weak-band entry boundary; the threshold was always correct, only the formula was wrong). The parameter is still named `cosineDistance` (matching `CandidateMatch.cosineDistance` field; rename would cascade through many call sites and is deferred). Test fixtures in `discovery-eval-helpers.test.ts` updated to use the corrected formula reference points (L2=√2 → score 0.5 for orthogonal vectors; L2=√0.6 → score 0.85 for strong-band entry; L2=√1.2 → score 0.7 for confident-band entry). Empirical verification: the offline BLAKE3 provider produces M1=100% post-fix (per PR #268's measurement) — only consistent with the formula being the dominant bug for symmetric-text-derivation cases, NOT consistent with the previously-cited "text asymmetry" diagnosis (which would have produced random embeddings under BLAKE3 → M1≪100%). **Implications for `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002`:** the corpus-size framing remains valid (N=5 too small); the symmetry-violation framing is downgraded from primary contamination source to secondary concern. `DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002` (store/query text derivation difference) IS a real violation but has measurably small impact on M1 once the formula is fixed. `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY` (#270) remains worthwhile (D2 ADR's API surface) but is no longer THE prereq for the v3 IMPL gate; corpus expansion (#269) is the single critical-path prereq. **Implications for `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX-001`:** that DEC's threshold-lowering was an incorrect fix for the actual bug. -001 is marked superseded in the source-code header docstring; the row is preserved for audit-trail purposes and shows that "we tried fix-A first and it papered over the bug; -002 is the actual fix." | Source: operator-led diagnosis review of PR #268 (which closed against current main as duplicate of PR #267 but had the correct diagnosis). vec0 distance-metric verified empirically at `packages/registry/src/schema.ts:95-100` (initial migration) and `:215-220` (migration 2 — keyed on spec_hash). Both vec0 declarations specify `embedding FLOAT[384]` with no `distance=cosine` annotation; per sqlite-vec documentation, that defaults to L2 Euclidean. Re-running unit tests post-fix: 185/193 pass (8 skipped for offline-provider gating); all 14 previously-failing tests in `discovery-eval-helpers.test.ts` updated to reference the corrected formula's points. Cornerstones preserved: cosine still never decides selection (#4); registry monotonic (#6); no versioning of the constant (it's a single value, atomically updated). Cross-references: `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D3-001` (formula now correctly reproduces D3's [0,1] band semantics), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-001` (Q1 threshold = 0.50 restored), `DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002` (relegated to secondary concern), `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002` (gate criteria amended in this row above). |
| DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-002 | **2026-05-10 — operator deferral, amends `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001` measurement-first gate.** **NOTE: this row's diagnosis-related framing is partially superseded by `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX-002` (filed shortly after this row).** The actual root cause of the contaminated [1.02, 1.16] distance range was the L2-as-cosine units bug, not text asymmetry — see -002. The CORPUS-SIZE amendment in this row remains valid; the SYMMETRY-VIOLATION framing is downgraded from primary contamination source to secondary concern. The two-prereq gate amendment stands: corpus expansion (#269) and symmetric-query API (#270 — also valuable as the D2 ADR's API surface) both ship before the gate fires. PR #267 produced post-calibration M1=80% on the seed-derived 5-entry subset of a 9-entry corpus and recommended pausing v3 IMPL. **Operator declines that recommendation as premature.** The N=5 measurement is contaminated by two orthogonal issues: (a) **sample size** — single-observation problem (one additional miss → 60% = FAIL); curated simple-shape queries don't exercise D1's multi-dim value proposition; threshold over-fit to this corpus's empirical distance distribution; (b) **L2-as-cosine units bug** (per `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX-002`; this row originally cited "store/query text asymmetry" as the dominant secondary cause — that diagnosis was incorrect and has been superseded), pushing distances on correct hits into [1.02, 1.16] instead of the natural [0, 0.5] range. PR #267's lowered M1 threshold (0.50 → 0.40) papered over (b) but did not fix it. **Amendment to `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001` measurement-first gate:** the gate fires only after BOTH of (1) `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-CORPUS-SEED` (#269, FuckGoblin) — stratified 50-100 query corpus across 5 categories executed against the **full yakcc shave registry** (~1,773+ atoms) AND (2) `WI-V3-DISCOVERY-IMPL-QUERY` (#270, Wrath) — symmetric canonicalize-derivation via `findCandidatesByQuery` per D2 ADR, fixing `DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002` — both land and the D5 harness is re-run on the corrected inputs. **PR #267's "pause v3 IMPL" recommendation is explicitly retracted** at the operator level; the technical work in PR #267 (calibration investigation, threshold amendment, helper unit tests, M5 scope fix) stands and is correct for the contaminated state. The 5-category stratification (behavior-only / guarantees-stressed / error-condition-stressed / non-functional-stressed / multi-aspect) IS the experimental design — per-category M1 numbers are the actual decision input. If single-vector hits ≥80% on category (1) but <80% on category (5), multi-dim has empirical justification; if single-vector hits ≥80% across ALL categories, multi-dim is unjustified at any storage cost. The `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001` 5× storage cost framing remains the rejection criterion; only the gate's INPUT requirements are amended. | Source: operator deferral 2026-05-10 in response to PR #267 recommendation. The original measurement-first guardrail was correctly motivated (don't ship 5× storage cost without empirical justification) but the gate's input criteria were under-specified — it didn't lock down corpus size, stratification, or symmetry-bug-free measurement. PR #267 surfaced the gap by producing a "PASS" recommendation on data that doesn't actually support a load-bearing decision. This amendment locks the gate's input requirements explicitly so future "PASS" or "FAIL" reads against the gate are statistically defensible. The 5-category stratification specifically targets D1's multi-dim value proposition: D1 only matters if queries actually stress different aspects (guarantees vs error conditions vs non-functional). Testing only category-1 queries is testing in conditions where D1 has no value-add by construction. The full-yakcc-registry stored side (per operator preference) provides realistic distractor density for precision/recall measurement; smaller corpora are toy conditions. Cornerstones preserved: cosine never decides selection (#4); registry monotonicity untouched (#6); no versioning of the corpus once committed (#1). Cross-references: `DEC-V3-INITIATIVE-001` (gate this amends), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-CALIBRATION-FIX-001` (the threshold amendment that surfaced the gap), `DEC-VECTOR-RETRIEVAL-002` (symmetry rule that #270 makes machine-enforced), `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D5-001` (corpus shape ADR which #269 implements). |

| DEC-BOOTSTRAP-MANIFEST-ACCUMULATE-001 | **WI-BOOTSTRAP-MANIFEST-ACCUMULATE (#284, 2026-05-10).** `bootstrap/expected-roots.json` is a **monotonic accumulator** — it never shrinks. Three sub-decisions: **(a) Additive merge:** `yakcc bootstrap` loads prior entries from the committed manifest before writing. Prior entries absent from the current shave are RETAINED (archived atoms from deleted branches/PRs). New shaved entries are ADDED. Result is the union sorted by `blockMerkleRoot` ASC. Summary line: `bootstrap: prior=N, shaved=M, added=K, total=N+K`. **(b) Superset `--verify` semantics:** PASS if `current_shave ⊆ committed_manifest` (archived atoms in committed but not in current shave are EXPECTED, never a failure). FAIL if any shaved atom is absent from committed (unrecorded new atoms) — error message names each missing root explicitly (Sacred Practice #5: loud failure). Supersedes the old byte-identity gate (`DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-VERIFY-001`). **(c) CI is the sole writer:** implementers MUST NOT run `yakcc bootstrap` manually to update the manifest. `.github/workflows/bootstrap-accumulate.yml` is the only writer; it runs on every PR and every push to main, pushing the updated manifest directly to main's `expected-roots.json`. `cancel-in-progress: false` — every PR's atoms must be recorded. Annotated as `@decision DEC-BOOTSTRAP-MANIFEST-ACCUMULATE-001` in `packages/cli/src/commands/bootstrap.ts`. | PR #280 deleted the in-house TS→WASM lowerer (~25,880 LoC). Atoms from that source existed in `bootstrap/expected-roots.json` on feature branches that never merged to main (most recent: commit `4c18f3c`, 2,619 entries). Re-running bootstrap against current HEAD would silently drop them, violating the registry's monotonic invariant: atoms are never deleted. The `bootstrap/expected-roots.json` is the registry's ground truth for "every atom ever shaved from this codebase" — its monotonicity is what makes the self-hosting demo (`yakcc bootstrap --verify` round-trips 100% of corpus per WI-V2-09) a meaningful claim rather than a vacuous one. Sub-decision (b) is the essential companion: the old byte-identity gate would fail on any run where the source tree has changed (e.g., archived atoms from deleted source) — replacing it with a superset check is the only semantics that are consistent with a monotonic accumulator. Sub-decision (c) prevents human error from shrinking the manifest by running `yakcc bootstrap` locally (the additive merge would prevent shrinkage, but CI ownership makes the intent explicit and auditable). Cross-references: `DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-VERIFY-001` (superseded for the equality gate; `:memory:` isolation pattern retained), `DEC-V2-BOOTSTRAP-MANIFEST-001` (entry schema unchanged), `DEC-CI-OFFLINE-001` (offline bootstrap embedding provider unchanged). |

| DEC-HOOKS-BASE-SUBSTITUTE-SMALL-GAP-001 | **WI-HOOKS-BASE-TEST-DISCOVERY-FIX (#342, 2026-05-10).** Float-tolerance buffer (`GAP_FLOAT_TOLERANCE = 1e-9`) added to the D2 gap-threshold comparison in `decideToSubstitute()`. **Root cause:** IEEE 754 double-precision arithmetic produces `0.15000000000000002` (one ULP above 0.15) when evaluating `0.90 - 0.75`, a mathematically-exact 0.15 gap. The D2 design intent (from `DEC-V3-DISCOVERY-D2-001`) is that gaps AT the boundary should REJECT substitution (inclusive boundary). Without the tolerance the comparison `gap <= 0.15` evaluated as `0.15000000000000002 <= 0.15 = false` and incorrectly substituted. **Fix:** `gap <= AUTO_ACCEPT_GAP_THRESHOLD + GAP_FLOAT_TOLERANCE` where `GAP_FLOAT_TOLERANCE = 1e-9`. Rationale for `1e-9`: ~7 orders of magnitude above `Number.EPSILON` (~2.2e-16), ~7 orders of magnitude below the smallest meaningful practical score difference (scores have 2 decimal places of precision). This eliminates the IEEE boundary artifact without changing any operator-observable behavior at any real score pair. **How the bug was surfaced:** the three `src/*.props.test.ts` files (`index.props.test.ts`, `substitute.props.test.ts`, `telemetry.props.test.ts`) were silently excluded from vitest discovery because `vitest.config.ts` glob was `test/**/*.test.ts` and these files lived in `src/`. The exclusion was discovered during WI-HOOKS-BASE-TEST-DISCOVERY-FIX (#341/#342 verification). **Resolution — test file placement:** all three props test files moved from `src/` to `test/` via `git mv`; relative imports updated from `./foo.props.js` to `../src/foo.props.js`. The vitest config `include` glob is NOT widened to `src/**` (would break the `test/`-only convention). **Regression test:** concrete boundary test added to `test/substitute.test.ts` exercising top-1=0.90, top-2=0.75 (mathematical gap=0.15, IEEE 754 gap=0.15000000000000002); asserts `substitute=false`. Annotated as `@decision DEC-HOOKS-BASE-SUBSTITUTE-SMALL-GAP-001` on `GAP_FLOAT_TOLERANCE` constant and comparison site in `packages/hooks-base/src/substitute.ts`. | Source: WI-HOOKS-BASE-TEST-DISCOVERY-FIX (#342). The latent IEEE 754 bug in `decideToSubstitute` was present since the D2 threshold comparison was written but was untestable while the property test that covered it (`prop_decideToSubstitute_small_gap_is_false`) was silently excluded from vitest. The `1e-9` tolerance value is chosen conservatively: (a) it is large enough to absorb any single-ULP subtraction error on values in [0,1] with 2-decimal precision; (b) it is small enough that no real-world score pair can be "close enough to the boundary" at this precision — scores produced by `candidatesToCombinedScores` are deterministic and their differences cluster near 0, 0.05, 0.10, 0.15, etc. with no sub-nanosecond-precision sensitivity. Alternative considered and rejected: rounding gap to 10 decimal places before comparison — rejected because arbitrary rounding introduces its own class of boundary artifacts at the rounding point. Alternative considered and rejected: changing `<=` to `<` (exclusive boundary) — rejected because D2's design intent is inclusive rejection at the boundary (ambiguous cases at the boundary should NOT substitute). The 51-test delta (84→135) when the props files are correctly discovered is the empirical proof that the glob exclusion was a real discovery gap, not a test-count anomaly. |
| DEC-BENCH-B5-SLICE1-001 | **WI-BENCHMARK-B5 Slice 1 (#189, 2026-05-10).** B5 multi-turn coherence benchmark Slice 1 — infrastructure, rubric, conversation seeds, offline classifier. **Scope:** Slice 1 does NOT call a real LLM or LLM-judge; it is the scaffold that Slices 2+3 plug into. **Three sub-decisions: (A) OFFLINE SIMULATION:** assistant_emission_target fields in conversations.jsonl serve as simulated LLM output for Slice 1. SHA-256 fingerprint in corpus-spec.json. **Pass/KILL bars (from #189):** mean ≥ 4.0 (PASS) / < 2.5 (KILL); subsequent-turn rate ≥ 90%; catastrophic ≤ 5% (PASS) / > 15% (KILL). **Methodology tradeoff:** programmatic classifier chosen over LLM-judge for Slice 1 for cost/speed (instant, zero API cost); LLM-judge added in Slice 2 for precision on ambiguous cases. Human rater deferred to Slice 3 or separate WI. Without B5, the contract-surfacing mechanism (inline contract comment) is un-validated. Slice 1 is an infrastructure WI — its job is to produce non-trivial programmatic output (the classifier must return non-uniform scores across the 10 seed conversations) and verify the harness wiring (`executeRegistryQueryWithSubstitution` called correctly via D-HOOK-6 embedded library call, not subprocess). Slice 2 is where real LLM emission replaces the simulation and the classifier's calibration is tested against actual model behavior. The three-slice structure is intentional: shipping a half-built benchmark harness as "done" is worse than shipping nothing (misleads future operators into thinking the verdict is available). | DEC-BENCH-B8-SYNTHETIC-SLICE1-001 | **WI-BENCHMARK-B8-SYNTHETIC Slice 1 (#192, 2026-05-11).** B8-SYNTHETIC foundation: transcript fixtures + hit-rate simulator + token-savings heuristic + f=1.0 ceiling run. **Three sub-decisions: (A) HIT RULE:** CONFIDENT_THRESHOLD (0.70) from @yakcc/hooks-base/yakcc-resolve.ts is the hit gate — consistent with the production substitution-decision threshold (D3 ADR §Q4 confident band). Lower threshold would inflate hits; higher would deflate. This keeps synthetic numbers aligned with what the real hook would actually substitute. **(B) TOKEN SAVINGS HEURISTIC:** Hook substitution output cost modeled as ~45 tokens (contract comment ~30 + import ~10 + binding ~5 per D-HOOK-4 format). Per-block: if hit, hook_tokens=45; if miss, hook_tokens=raw_tokens. This is a CEILING calculation — production may be slightly different per atom name/signature length. **(C) D1 GATE CLARIFICATION:** Issue body says "gated only on D1". D1 was decided NOT-shipping per #150 closing comments. Benchmark uses shipped single-vector schema (registry's actual current state). Scaling characteristics are independent of D1 shipping. **Slice 1 f=1.0 ceiling results (Windows x64, Ryzen 9 9950X, 2026-05-11):** Corpus N=10 (substrate=4, glue=3, application=3), registry 2103 specs. Hit rate (all tiers): 100.0% (every description finds a match above 0.70 threshold — registry is comprehensive). Mean savings % (all tasks): 9.2%. **Verdict: KILL** (< 50% KILL bar). **Root cause of KILL:** Substrate-tier tiny helpers (clamp 28 tokens, isSafeInt 22 tokens, padLeft 22 tokens) are SMALLER than the hook substitution overhead (~45 tokens) — substituting them adds tokens rather than saving them. Glue and application tier show healthy savings (21–48%). The architecture's token-savings value is block-size dependent: savings require raw_tokens >> 45. **Interpretation and consequence:** The KILL verdict at f=1.0 with 100% hit rate reflects the corpus composition (many small substrate helpers), not a fundamental flaw in the architecture. The benchmark is an honest measurement. Slice 2 must expand the corpus with larger, more realistic LLM emissions (complete function bodies with docstrings, error handling, type annotations) to test whether the savings ceiling becomes viable at more representative block sizes. The KILL criterion fires correctly; the replanning action is corpus calibration, not architecture replanning. Annotated as `@decision DEC-BENCH-B8-SYNTHETIC-SLICE1-001` in `bench/B8-synthetic/hit-rate-simulator.mjs` and `bench/B8-synthetic/run.mjs`. **Artifact:** `tmp/B8-synthetic/slice1-2026-05-11_22-16-45.json` (force-added). | Source: WI-BENCHMARK-B8-SYNTHETIC Slice 1 (#192). The f=1.0 single-point run is the ceiling measurement; Slice 2 adds the f-sweep curve.
